  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10980474268093643861">Magic, adventure, mystery, and romance combine in this epic debut in which a young princess must reclaim her dead mother’s throne, learn to be a ruler—and defeat the Red Queen, a powerful and malevolent sorceress determined to destroy her.<br/><br/>On her nineteenth birthday, Princess Kelsea Raleigh Glynn, raised in exile, sets out on a perilous journey back to the castle of her bir</span>
  <span id="freeText10980474268093643861" style="display:none">Magic, adventure, mystery, and romance combine in this epic debut in which a young princess must reclaim her dead mother’s throne, learn to be a ruler—and defeat the Red Queen, a powerful and malevolent sorceress determined to destroy her.<br /><br />On her nineteenth birthday, Princess Kelsea Raleigh Glynn, raised in exile, sets out on a perilous journey back to the castle of her birth to ascend her rightful throne. Plain and serious, a girl who loves books and learning, Kelsea bears little resemblance to her mother, the vain and frivolous Queen Elyssa. But though she may be inexperienced and sheltered, Kelsea is not defenseless: Around her neck hangs the Tearling sapphire, a jewel of immense magical power; and accompanying her is the Queen’s Guard, a cadre of brave knights led by the enigmatic and dedicated Lazarus. Kelsea will need them all to survive a cabal of enemies who will use every weapon—from crimson-caped assassins to the darkest blood magic—to prevent her from wearing the crown.<br /><br />Despite her royal blood, Kelsea feels like nothing so much as an insecure girl, a child called upon to lead a people and a kingdom about which she knows almost nothing. But what she discovers in the capital will change everything, confronting her with horrors she never imagined. An act of singular daring will throw Kelsea’s kingdom into tumult, unleashing the vengeance of the tyrannical ruler of neighboring Mortmesne: the Red Queen, a sorceress possessed of the darkest magic. Now Kelsea will begin to discover whom among the servants, aristocracy, and her own guard she can trust.<br /><br />But the quest to save her kingdom and meet her destiny has only just begun—a wondrous journey of self-discovery and a trial by fire that will make her a legend . . . if she can survive.<br /><br />This book will be a beautifully designed package with illustrated endpapers, a map of the Tearling, and a ribbon marker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10980474268093643861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29048273-chris-reisor"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29048273-chris-reisor">Chris Reisor</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Besides the violence, there is pedophilia and I guess what you'd refer to as sex magick? Lots and lots of rape (more personal and descriptive in the 2<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Besides the violence, there is pedophilia and I guess what you'd refer to as sex magick? Lots and lots of rape (more personal and descriptive in the 2nd book) and white slavery. Children drugged so that a monster can suck the blood out of their bodies.<br /><br />If you're cool with lines like: "Pine wakes me up at three in the morning and tells me you're ready for me. I go to your chamber and get to lick Petra's c#$t for your pleasure" for your young adult, then I guess, sure... it's a young adult book.<br /><br />I'm being sarcastic... this is totally inappropriate for young adults. I'm not sure how other folks here can find a way to compare this to Lord of the Rings; in terms of thematic content and simple literary quality, this isn't even the same ballpark.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi! I don't think I would call it like Game of Thrones. It has a lot of politics in it, and the consequences of everything the main character chooses <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi! I don't think I would call it like Game of Thrones. It has a lot of politics in it, and the consequences of everything the main character chooses to do as a queen. It has some violence, but you can't really compare it to the show, it's not gory. I loved this book! It was so interesting and so realistic, I had really high expectation and it did not disappoint!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_794739969" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794739969" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794739969?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593072691" href="/book/show/17415882-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=weight-issues">weight-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=try-hard">try-hard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794739969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17988968006880317151"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>What does [that lady] see when she looks in the mirror? Kelsea wondered. How could a woman who looked so old still place so much importance on being attractive? Kelsea saw now that there was something far worse than being ugly: being ugly and thinking you were beautiful.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Because how DARE anyone ugly have confidence in themselves.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/625186.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I die, I want inscribed on my gravestone "She Read <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i>." Call me unambitious, but that shall be counted among my proudest accomplis</span>
  <span id="freeText17988968006880317151" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>What does [that lady] see when she looks in the mirror? Kelsea wondered. How could a woman who looked so old still place so much importance on being attractive? Kelsea saw now that there was something far worse than being ugly: being ugly and thinking you were beautiful.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Because how DARE anyone ugly have confidence in themselves.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/625186.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I die, I want inscribed on my gravestone "She Read <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i>." Call me unambitious, but that shall be counted among my proudest accomplishments, because never have I ever read a more painfully long, worthless book.<br><br>The copywriter who wrote this book's summary compares it to <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>Game of Thrones</i>; they have clearly read neither. <b>They compared to the world-building to that of <i>The Hunger Games</i>. They compared the characters to that of <i>Game of Thrones</i>.</b><br><br>Are you fucking kidding me?<br><br>A thousand monkeys typing on a thousand typewriters could write a book that is more similar to those works than anything this book has to offer.<br><br>This was also the most intensely painful reading experience I have ever had due to the sheer length of the book, aggravated by the fact that the book just dragged on and on and on without a point. <b>This is the book that doesn't end.</b> A good 30% of the book is devoted to traveling. Not since <i>The Hobbit</i> have I been so fucking bored out of my mind. Bilbo Baggins could have gone there and back again, and then make another round around Middle Earth, and sure, why not---take a few years to flutter around Rivendell chilling with the elves in the time it took this book to go anywhere.<br><br><u>The Summary</u>: Kelsea Raleigh is the new Queen of the Tearling. Her mother, the late Queen Elyssa has died, and it is time for Kelsea to claim the throne. She travels to the new kingdom. She's traveling. She's on a horse. They're slowly making their way to the castle. Slooooooooowly.<br><br>Meanwhile, the Red Queen of Mortmesne is wonder where the fuck Kelsea is. She's spent the last 19 years searching for her. Seriously, where the fuck is the girl? Oh, well, the Red Queen will think about that later. Time to fuck some slaves! OH YEAH. GIVE IT TO ME, BABY.<br><br>Kelsea's still traveling. Man, her new guards are really, really good looking. Oh, shit, she's kidnapped. But not really, because the kidnappers pretty much let Kelsea wander free.<br><br>Oh, whew. She's free. Back to traveling! Whooo! OH YAY, WE'RE AT THE CASTLE. Kelsea makes some fucking stupid decisions and pretty much dooms her country within hours of reaching her new castle.<br><br>Meanwhile, Javel, the guard, is telling his story, his sad story of how his wife was lost to him. <br><br>Kelsea's throned queen! YAY! She spends a lot of time talking to her advisors. She almost gets killed (several times).<br><br>Meanwhile, the priest, Father Tyler, is really, really upset at how his life gets flipped turned upside down.<br><br>The Red Queen of Montmesne is fucking more slaves. Where is that dratted Kelsea.<br><br>Kelsea thinks she is very plain. She should go on a diet. But no, she shouldn't, because she's plain anyway, and who cares about appearances, anyway. Man, Kelsea wishes she were pretty. As pretty as her maidservant, the one whose beauty is so valued that she got enslaved and raped for it.<br><br>Meanwhile, Javel is still doing shit. Talking to people. Getting roped into some random-ass plans.<br><br>Father Tyler is still moping around.<br><br>The Red Queen's pissed off. That fucking Kelsea. Why does she keep eluding my grasp. And by grasp, the Red Queen means her minion's grasps, since the Red Queen is just too important to do anything about hunting Kelsea herself. Magic, pfft. Ugh, whatever. Let's get ourselves a 7-year old little boy and BLEEP him in the BLEEP BLEEP. That is so not legal.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390977720ra/8310424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Javel's still talking somehow.<br><br>Kelsea's still talking to people. It sure would be nice if she were pretty. But really, Kelsea doesn't have time to think about that right now. There are more important things at hand. Like insulting a woman in front of the Royal Court.<br><br>Fuck, they're traveling AGAIN?!<br><br>The end.<br><br><b>765. Mother. Fucking. Pages.</b><br><br><u>The Setting</u>: IT DOESN'T MAKE ANY MOTHERFUCKING SENSE. <b>I started this book thinking it was a medieval fantasy. It wasn't.</b> It has an old-world feel. It's not. Women are in long dresses. We are riding horses. We're using hawks to hunt. There are kings and queens and magic and castles. What you you mean it's not in the past? What do you mean it's not a fantasy.<br><br><b>THIS IS THE FUTURE? THIS IS A DYSTOPIA? WE USED TO BE THE UNITED STATES AND EUROPE? WHAT THE ACTUAL FUCK? WHAT HAPPENED?</b><br><br>I seriously do not fucking understand this setting. First off, it is fucking lazy, because the retelling of the history is told by mouth, AS A STORY.<blockquote>
  <i>“Once upon a time, there was a kingdom called the Tearling. It was founded by a man named William Tear, a utopian who dreamed of a land of plenty for all. But ironically, the Tearling was a kingdom of scarce resources, for the British and Americans had not been fortunate in their choice of landing place."</i>
</blockquote>British. American. This is the motherfucking future, people. How the fuck did we get here? And more importantly. WHERE ARE WE?<br><br>Why are all technologies lost? We supposedly got to this place in an event called <b>The Crossing</b>. Where is this place? Are we even on Earth? Why are there so few survivors? This land is called New Europe. We have a town called New London. Did it actually pop up out of the ocean? Why was the old world destroyed? Why did we have to seek refuge in New Europe? Are we so fucking inconsistent that in all the hundreds of fucking years in which we've settled here that we have lost all the motherfucking techologies of today's time in the future. So much that we don't even have the technology for motherfucking PRINTING PRESSES? We have geneticists. But we don't have the technology to buy books.<br><br>And why are books rare? <b>Because we motherfucking burned them for fuel when we got here. Despite the motherfucking forests of oaks that surrounds this new land, they fucking burned BOOKS for fuel.</b><blockquote>
  <i>That was what had happened to most of the books that originally came over in the British-American Crossing: the desperate had burned them for fuel or warmth.</i>
</blockquote>There are no doctors. There are, like, 2 doctors in the whole of fucking New London. New civilizations have come up with technology, they've been so much more innovative than this. <b>The Medieval Ages were more advanced than the Tearling, because they don't know how to fucking make gunpowder or cannons.</b><br><br>Seriously. You expect us to retain absolutely fucking NOTHING of the knowledge that we have gained for all these years? Did you choose the motherfucking dumbest pieces of shits to carry over to the New World? Why didn't you choose important people, like scientists, botanists, doctors, instead of a bunch of fucking feeblewitted morons who don't know how to carry over fucking technology from the old world when you crossed over to the new. Who fucking BURN BOOKS FOR FUEL DESPITE BEING SURROUNDED BY TREES.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390977720ra/8310425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fucking dystopian fail.<br><br><u>The Writing</u>: Not since Charles Dickens have I read such verbosity. <b>There is a reason why this book is so long. It is packed to the brim with the most long-winded, irrelevant description of every fucking thing in the world.</b><br><br>Introspection? Sure. This book has it aplenty. <b>Let's describe every single fucking thought that Kelsea has ever fucking had in her head.</b> Kelsea thinks. A lot. Some relevant things. Mostly very, very, very idiotic things that make no fucking different whether they were omitted or not.<blockquote>
  <i>Red hair was a recessive gene, and in the three centuries since the Crossing, it had bred slowly and steadily out of the population. Carlin had told Kelsea that some women, and even some men, liked to dye their hair red, since the rare commodity was always valuable. But after about an hour of sneaking looks at the guard, Kelsea became certain that she was looking at a true head of red hair. No dye was that good.</i>
</blockquote>Her dreams? Kelsea thinks about them. Her opinions about the men? Sure, let's have it. Kelsea's insecurity? Sure, let's have several fucking paragraphs on it. Man, her food just tastes fucking terrible tonight. <b>Let's describe her thoughts on the venison in excruciating detail.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Dinner was venison, stringy and only barely edible after roasting over the fire. The deer must have been very old. Kelsea had seen only a few birds and squirrels on their ride through the Reddick, though the greenery was very lush; there could be no lack of water. Kelsea wanted to ask the men about the lack of animals, but she worried that it would be taken as a complaint about the meal.</i>
</blockquote>Man, it's a motherfucking long journey. After all, the traveling alone takes about 30% of the book. LET'S JUST DESCRIBE EVERY SINGLE FREAKING DETAIL ON IT. The houses are built with bricks. LET'S DESCRIBE THE FUCKING BRICKS IN DETAIL.<blockquote>
  <i>To the east, Kelsea spotted what must be the house of a noble: a high tower made of red brick. Real brick! Tearling brick was a notoriously poor building material compared to Mortmesne’s, which was made with better mortar and commanded at least a pound per kilo. Carlin had an oven made of real bricks, built for her by Barty, and Kelsea had wondered more than once whether Barty had bought the bricks off the black market from Mortmesne.</i>
</blockquote>DETAILS! DETAILS! DETAILS! We are fucking drowning in details. The clothes of the noblemen! Let's decribe them! One of the ladies wear a hat in the shape of a fish! Let's mention that. And while we're at it, let's make fun of her for it! WILL IT EVER STOP?!<br><br><u>The Guards</u>: Not since <i>Monty Python and the Holy Grail</i> have there ever been such irreverent, incompetent fucking royal guards. They are the most fucking pathetic examples of soldiers I have ever fucking encountered. This is Kelsea. She is one of the last of her royal line. Her life is priceless. She is supposed to be guarded by 9 men. 9 men who are motherfucking blundering assholes because they cannot do anything right.<br><br>While they are traveling, the men get drunk and sing bawdy songs instead of securing her guard. They are completely fucking shocked that later on in the journey, they are captured.<br><br>While they are traveling, they are caught AGAIN off their guard. Kelsea is forced to flee for her life.<br><br>At the castle, while they are supposed to be watching her back. Kelsea gets stabbed---in the back.<blockquote>
  <i>...a bolt of pain arrowed all the way down to her toes.<br>Stabbed, she thought, dazed. Mace didn’t cover my back after all.</i>
</blockquote>Later on, in the bath, Kelsea gets cornered by an assassin! She's almost fucking killed again.<br><br>WHERE ARE THE FUCKING NITWITS GUARDING HER?!<br><br>Guards?! Guards?! They are supposed to be subservient. They are supposed to be respectful. They are supposed to be odebient. They are not supposed to talk back to her. Oh, sure, they SAY they're not going to talk back to her.<blockquote>
  <i>He stared at her without expression. “I say nothing, Lady. That’s why I’m a Queen’s Guard.”</i>
</blockquote>But words mean fucking nothing. Because whatever Mace (real name Lazarus, head of Kelsea's guard) is, it's not fucking subservient. He talks down to her, as if she were an incompetent little girl (well, she is, but she is still the fucking queen). He talks back to her. He disagrees with her. When she's gravely injured, Mace nudges her by poking at her with his foot. Is this the behavior of a guard towards his queen? I don't think so.<blockquote>
  <i>Mace’s boot landed in the small of her back, and Kelsea bit her tongue against a scream.</i>
</blockquote><u>Kelsea</u>: Incompetent nitwit. <b>A heroine who is so astoundingly stupid and unprepared by her fucking mentors that she is unworthy of governing anything but a toy kingdom made of Legos.</b><br><br>I hope Kelsea steps on the pieces. I hope they hurt badly. I hope our aspiring queen is in pain for the torment and the headache and the hangover I experienced while reading this book about one of the most insipid heroine to ever litter the precious pages of a book.<br><br>She constantly complains about how plain she is. <blockquote>
  <i>But her face was as round and ruddy as a tomato, and—there was no other word for it—plain.</i>
</blockquote>She has the most fucking idiotic thoughts about everything and everything. No subject is too minor for her notice. The rug? Oh, it's probably made of deer hide. Spare me.<br><br>She is not a fucking queen. Her guardians are incompetent, because she has been so completely fucking sheltered from the world that she doesn't understand anything, but she still knows things. Somehow. She has never seen alcohol, yet she knows what alcohol smells like. She knows what alcoholism looks like when she sees it in a man. And she revels in being drunk, cause it's just like in a book, y'all!<blockquote>
  <i>Kelsea woke with an aching head and a parched mouth, but it wasn’t until breakfast that she realized it was her first hangover. Despite the discomfort, she was charmed to experience something that she’d only read about in a book. An upset stomach was a small price to pay for fiction made real.</i>
</blockquote>She cares SO MUCH for the fate of her people. Kelsea is so incredibly hurt that her people are being sent as slaves to Mortmesne---250 a month---that she is willing to renege on the treaty between their countries. <b>Within hours of her arrival to the capital, Kelsea makes a heroic gesture that completely endangers the peace of two nations.</b> She stops the shipment of slaves. She was warned. She didn't listen. She risks the lives of the entire nation for the sake of a few.<blockquote>
  <i>“Lady, the Mort Treaty is specific. There is no appeals process, no outside arbiter. If a single shipment fails to arrive in Demesne on time, the Mort Queen has the right to invade this country and wreak terror. I lived through the last Mort invasion, Lady, and I assure you, Mhurn wasn’t exaggerating the carnage. Before you take action, consider the consequences.”</i>
</blockquote>Despite being plain, Kelsea is terribly judgmental of looks. She criticizes an old, ugly woman for daring to look beautiful. She is envious of another woman's beauty, despite the fact that that woman's beauty got her raped.<br><br>Kelsea complains a lot about the extravagances at court. The pointless waste of money. So much that she is willing to waste her valuable men's time and her own resources into traveling 2 weeks to get her books from her old home. And right away. It must be done right away.<br><br><u>The Fetch</u>: A criminal. The projected love interest. <b>A Robin Hood? Not quite. You see, Robin Hood steals from the rich and actually DISTRIBUTES it to the poor.</b> The Fetch? Nah.<blockquote>
  <i>“Well, he’s a hero to the common people, Lady. Every piece of rich man’s fortune lost endears him to the poor.”<br>“Does he distribute the money to the poor?”<br>“No, Lady.”</i>
</blockquote>So, um. Exactly HOW is he the hero of the common people?<br><br>Naturally, she should turn him in. Kelsea is the queen, she should set an example to her people. Put criminals where they belong.<br><br>Or not.<blockquote>
  <i>Kelsea took a deep breath. “I wouldn’t betray him for any number of pounds.”<br>“Ah, Christ.”</i>
</blockquote>Emma, Emma Watson. I heard that you have signed up for this project. I adore you. You are brilliant. You are gorgeous. You are a goddess, and you have won my heart ever since you stepped onto the screens of Harry Potter, with your disapproving frown and your frizzy hair, far more beautiful than Hermione Watson could ever be. But I adored you then, I love you now, and <b>I hope for your sake that the movie adaptation exceeds every aspect of the book, because the book itself has almost no substance to offer</b>.<br><br>I can't even hate this book because it tries so hard. It is the equivalent of having your 6-year old niece draw a picture of you. Sure, you look like a motherfucking moose with butterfly wings for some fucking reason, but hey, it's an A for effort, right?<br><br><i>Quotes were taken from an uncorrected galley proof subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>

<div id="review_965289729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965289729" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965289729?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21792577-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965289729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15702695976642985309">$1.99 today on Amazon!<br/><br/><b> Definitely one of the Top 10 of my 2014 favorites!</b><br/>Word of warning, though...<br/>I'm seeing tons of 1 star reviews. Evidently, this is one of those <b>Love it or Hate It</b> books. I've pawed over the other reviews, and I'm honestly not connecting with any of the other reviewers' problems with this one.<br/>I didn't think the heroine had low self-esteem.<br/>I didn't think parts of it were far-fetched or full of plot holes.<br/>I didn't think it resembled other books (maybe because I haven't read th</span>
  <span id="freeText15702695976642985309" style="display:none">$1.99 today on Amazon!<br /><br /><b> Definitely one of the Top 10 of my 2014 favorites!</b><br />Word of warning, though...<br />I'm seeing tons of 1 star reviews. Evidently, this is one of those <b>Love it or Hate It</b> books. I've pawed over the other reviews, and I'm honestly not connecting with any of the other reviewers' problems with this one.<br />I didn't think the heroine had low self-esteem.<br />I didn't think parts of it were far-fetched or full of plot holes.<br />I didn't think it resembled other books (maybe because I haven't read them?).<br /><b>But</b>...and this is kind of a huge thing, I guess...<br />I also didn't read the blurb.<br />So, I had no idea this was supposed to be the next Hunger Games/ Game of Thrones hybrid.<br />And it probably wouldn't have mattered even if I had.<br />Hunger Games is nowhere near a favorite of mine, and neither is Game of Thrones.<br />They're both good books, but neither one blew me out of the water.<br />To each his own and all that stuff.<br />I said all that to say this:<br />I loved it, but that certainly doesn't mean you will. <br /><br />What surprised me the most about this one was that the heroine was just a truly <i>good</i> person. She saw something happening that was wrong, and instead of doing that thing where they have to work behind the scenes to fix it, she just put her foot down and put a stop to it.<br /><i>Sure, we're gonna start a war with an unbelievably powerful country that is probably going to wipe us off the map...but I'm not going to send kids in cages to be used as sex slaves to avoid the war.</i><br />Huh?<br />That just doesn't happen in most of the books I've read.<br />Most of the time, the hero/heroine hates what's going on, and <i>eventually</i> puts a stop to it. But not immediately. Like, the first second they get a whiff of power. Someone talks them out of doing something rash without considering the consequences, yadda, yadda, yadda.<br /><br />Also, the heroine isn't attractive, thin, or magically endowed with assassin skills.<br />And, yes, several times she mentions that she wishes she were beautiful like some of the women around her.<br />I'm seeing lots of complaints about how she should have been super-duper-happy with not being a bombshell.<br />Why?<br />I thought it added a touch of realism. When I was younger, I worried about my looks, and I compared myself to other women. Most of the time, I thought I was somehow lacking. <br />Did that make me a bad person? <br />Should I be ashamed to admit that? <br /><i>Pssssht.</i><br />Whatever. Everyone deals with that emotion. Why can't an otherwise strong female character be allowed to have those thoughts?<br />I would have a problem with it if she let it interfere with doing the right thing. <br />She didn't, so I didn't either.<br /><br />Personally, I didn't want to put this book down. I got sucked into it, and couldn't let it go. <br />I loved the magical elements to it. The stones played a large role in the book, and I'm interested to find out what exactly is the backstory on those things.<br />And tons of folks are going to disagree with this, but I loved that this had some unexplained post-apocalyptic thing that happened in the past. The fact that this supposedly takes place in a medieval<i>ish</i> setting, but sometime in the <i>future</i>, was one of the highlights for me. I wanna know more about what happened during this Crossing!<br />Still, the best part of the book was the lack of romance.<br />None. Zip, zilch, zero, nada.<br />If it's coming, it's certainly going to be a slow-burn, and I'm more than ok with that.<br /><br />Last (<b>but very important</b>) thing?<br />I'm not sure why the hell this is getting labeled YA here on Goodreads. <br />It's not. <br />There are a lot of references to child rape, rape in general, a scene where a child is basically eaten alive by a monster, sex in every form (not fade to black), the f-bomb (among other things) gets dropped, a nipple get sliced, a woman gets burned alive, etc..<br />It's not something I'd feel comfortable handing to a younger teenager.<br /><br />I may be absolutely alone in loving this, but I thought it was fantastic!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15702695976642985309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8228794011850884008">For the most part I enjoyed this story. I think it was a solid start to this series, but I do feel like it was missing something. I'm interested to see where this trilogy goes! </span>

<div id="review_848334773" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848334773" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/848334773?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21792577-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=advanced-reader-copy">advanced-reader-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=coulda-been-better">coulda-been-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer848334773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5832230354385503513"><b>
  <u>28 Feb '14</u>
</b><br/><a href='http://elfswood.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a> | <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5548051-amanda%22' rel='nofollow noopener'>goodreads</a><br/><i>Disclaimer: This is a review of an uncorrected Advanced Reader Copy.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>Long rant ahead, folks. Don't say I didn't warn you.</b><br/><br/>So some time in the future of earth, when the world has gotten so messed up and irredeemable, a man named William Tear gathered up his people along with doctors, scientists, and other citizens of some value, and took them on a huge boat.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393656284i/8747054._SX540_.jpg' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>With the intention of building a new democratic civilization founded on world order and... socialism(?) William T</span>
  <span id="freeText5832230354385503513" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>28 Feb '14</u>
</b><br><a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5548051-amanda%22" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a><br><i>Disclaimer: This is a review of an uncorrected Advanced Reader Copy.</i><br><br><br><b>Long rant ahead, folks. Don't say I didn't warn you.</b><br><br>So some time in the future of earth, when the world has gotten so messed up and irredeemable, a man named William Tear gathered up his people along with doctors, scientists, and other citizens of some value, and took them on a huge boat.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393656284i/8747054._SX540_.jpg" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With the intention of building a new democratic civilization founded on world order and... socialism(?) William Tear and his people undertook the Great Crossing, where they crossed from......... America(?) and settled in the new, unknown land of......... England(?)<b>[*]</b><br><br>---------------<br><b>[*]</b> like for reals. Did the future magically grow new, unexplored continents? I mean, where did they sail off to? What happened to the continents they sailed away <i>from</i>? Did they just swim into a void and pop up in a completely different universe? like what is happening here guys, like help me out.<br>---------------<br><br>The people, having learnt nothing from the past, decided that a monarchy is absolutely the best way to achieve William Tear's socialist dreams, but unfortunately,<br><blockquote>
  <i>... it ended in bloody disaster with the assassination of Jonathan Tear</i>
</blockquote><br>upon which the Raleigh line took over the throne, and this envisioned utopia eventually devolved into something that took everyone but the reader by surprise.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393657316i/8747145._SY540_.jpg" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Then something about a war, a spineless queen, a formidable(?) enemy, and enter our special Kelsea.<br><br>Nothing of much importance happened. This book <b>served more as an introduction to Kelsea and her ascension to the throne</b>, and how amazing she is at it. <br>I won't rehash the rest of the book, because I put myself through the pain of reading it once, and I won't do it again. My experience reading this book was largely inexplicable ... something kept grating on my nerves until I sat down and actually pinpointed what it was that bothered me about the whole thing.<br><br>Now that I've figured it out, it's going to take rather long, so I'll point out the main issues I had with this book:<br><br>1) Convenient and Arbitrary Plot Devices<br>2) Trivialization of IMPORTANT STUFF<br>3) Appeal to Popular Sentiment<br>4) Weak and Clichéd Characterization<br><br><br>~*~<br><br><u>
  <b>&gt;&gt;CONVENIENT AND ARBITRARY PLOT DEVICES&lt;&lt;</b>
</u><br>Aspects of the world were inconsistent at times. People had talents or gifts only when they were convenient to the plot:<br><br>Andalie could only foresee events to the extent that it does not undermine the suspense in the narrative.<br><br>Lazarus could sense people's intentions and loyalty, and yet this talent disappears when it comes to the traitor amongst his men, or direct attacks upon Her Majesty's self.<br><br>How convenient that TWO of Kelsea's most loyal followers happen to even <i>have</i> such useful talents to begin with!<br><br><i>The Queen of the Tearling</i>'s plot conveniences are not limited to its characters, however. <b>The whole history of the realm was <i>built</i> upon convenience</b>; ever since the Great Crossing, where each person was allowed to bring one book, and yet <i>no one</i> thought of bringing something remotely science-y. <br>Instead, they brought <i>The Hobbit</i> and <b>JK Rowling</b> and <i>Lord of the Rings</i>.<br><br>So of course, how convenient that the doctors and scientists practically all died during some sort of terrible act of nature during the Crossing. How <i>convenient</i> that all former knowledge is gone, leaving us with a future filled with swords and horses and legit birth control and cigarettes.<br><br>Even what technologies are "forgotten" and what has been magically "resurrected" were completely arbitrary and at the author's whim. Give me a God. Damn. break.<br><br><br>~*~<br><br><u>
  <b>&gt;&gt;TRIVIALIZATION OF IMPORTANT STUFF&lt;&lt;</b>
</u><br>Now, I'll let you know that I have much patience for boring, tedious, Bilbo-Baggins-There-and-Back-Again sort of journeys. In fact, I <i>love</i> it when it is done right; when it sucks you in to this magical realm full of elves and dwarves, even though you never spend the journey meeting a single one. When it gives you an understanding of the world, its history, its people and many cultures...<br><br><i>The Queen of the Tearling</i>? Not so much. I kept waiting and waiting for a shed of light to reveal to me what on God's gracious earth happened to ... well, Earth ... and how it got to where they were now, but it never came.<br><br>The novel completely brushed aside the "minor details" as if it didn't matter. Well guess what, you can't just make allusions to the London Bridge, and New Europe, and <i>not</i> tell us what happened to <i>Old</i> Europe. <br>It made the whole worldbuilding rather irrelevant, really. What's the point of fashioning your novel after our very own earth, when the fate and history of our own world has fuck all to do with your story? Why not just come up with a completely new universe, slap dash your realms and characters and history into it, and be done with it all?<br>I suspect more will be revealed in the second book (it is a trilogy, after all), but by that time, frustrations are pretty damn high. One of <b>the purposes of a first book is to build the foundations of your world</b>. Well, we barely have a single pillar to hold <i>The Tearling</i> up.<br><br>Other smaller plot details were also largely ignored and "explained away" with a single sentence. The <b>author would much prefer using up word count on internal musings and philosophical reflections, rather than spending it on actual worldbuilding and characterization</b>.<br>It would take far too much time for us to come to trust Andalie through actual good character building skills, so instead the author takes the easy way out and uses Lazarus's "people-sensing" skills to provide yet another plot-device and add Andalie into Kelsea's most trusted followers without even a second thought.<br><br><br>~*~<br><br><u>
  <b>&gt;&gt;APPEAL TO POPULAR SENTIMENT&lt;&lt;</b>
</u><br>Oh Lord how this one frustrated me.<br><br>I'm not talking about the logical fallacy, I'm talking about how this book tried so hard to appeal to our emotions and contemporary attitudes. Forget name-dropping <b>Rowling</b> or <b>Tolkien</b>'s works of arts ... those are minor details that I can roll my eyes at and move on.<br><br>Instead, let's focus more on Kelsea<b>[*]</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393665009i/8748531.png" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>---------------<br><b>[*]</b>Sidenote. You're gonna have <b>Emma Watson</b> play plain-almost-ugly Kelsea?? Yeah okay.<br>---------------<br><br>Kelsea is this plain (and not in the "is-actually-beautiful-but-she-doesn't-know-it" kind of way) 19 year-old girl, who fights for her people, has compassion for the poor, and is concerned for the well-being and empowerment of women.<br><br>So believe me how guilty I feel for not liking her one bit. I must be some kind of devilspawn.<br><br>But every once in a while, Kelsea comes up with these gems that make me think-- <i>hang on a sec,</i> no I don't feel bad about hating her:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>How could a woman who looked so old still place so much importance on being attractive? (...) she saw now that there was something far worse than being ugly: being ugly and thinking you were beautiful.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>There are just <i>so many</i> things wrong with that one, singular sentence that once I read it, I stopped in my tracks and thought, Wait. This is a joke, right. The author <i>deliberately</i> made such an abhorrently judgmental, hypocritical (I'll get to that) character. Like, <i>on purpose</i>.<br><br>But no. <b>Kelsea -- and the way she is written -- just takes itself so seriously</b> that there could be no possible way we are supposed to <i>dislike</i> her for one bit. <br>Every single entity on the planet likes her, except for the agents of evil, whom we are automatically supposed to disprove of. Every single person values her courage, selflessness, and genuinely treats her like everything she does is so amazing, that there is no possible way us readers are supposed to condemn her for any trivial thing.<br><br>And then it all hit me, and I realized exactly what is wrong with Kelsea.<br><br>We are supposed to like her, not because she is an incredibly written character, who goes through hardships we can relate to, who has to make hard choices and sacrifices.<br><br><b>We are supposed to like her, simply for being <i>the only human being with a shred of decency</i> on the planet.</b> It isn't that she's so spectacularly kind-hearted and intelligent and cunning, it's just that everyone around her is so infinitely <i>un</i>likeable, it makes her look good. <br><br>We are supposed to be as "wow"ed and amazed as the villagers and Guards of Tear that this noble, caring girl suddenly pops out to lead them; but you know what, I don't buy it. Your previous leaders and figures of authority have really sucked, and I'm sorry. But don't try to pass off Kelsea as an incredible character, because technique- and narrative-wise, she isn't. <br><br>The book tries to appeal to its readers, willing us to like Kelsea because of her humanitarian qualities. Unfortunately, you don't get a cookie for upholding basic human fucking rights. Or shall I also thank the million men out there for <b>not</b> raping me?<br><br>So I'm not falling for your cheap ploy, <b>Johansen</b>. <br><br><br>~*~<br><br><u>
  <b>&gt;&gt;WEAK AND CLICHED CHARACTERIZATION&lt;&lt;</b>
</u><br>What you can expect in practically any fantasy novel nowadays:<br><br>- ALL nobles are shitheads<br>- The Church is corrupt EVIL incarnate<b>[*]</b><br>- The Kingdom is secretly poor<br>- There is an evil, magical enemy somewhere out there who for some reason hasn't killed you yet although you pose a great threat<br>- You probably don't know who your mother / father is<br><br>---------------<br><b>[*]</b>Speaking of the church, I realize it is <i>all the rage</i> nowadays to jab at religions and people who believe in "a fictional character watching from the sky", and the more and louder you jab, the more points you get.<br><i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> seems to be of the same mind, and as demonizing the Church is so in-fashion nowadays, that is exactly what <b>Johansen</b> did. <br><br>Don't get me wrong -- reading about atheist characters, reading about their thought processes and often musings against religion is fine by me. But there is a point where you say <b>enough!</b><br><br><blockquote>
<i>"(...) If you can tolerate my arguments, you're free to minister to or convert any other occupant of this Keep, not excepting the pigs and chickens."<br><br>"You make sport of my religion, Lady," (...)<br><br>"I make sport of all things inconsistent, Father."</i><br><br>*<br><br><i>Andalie pursed her lips (...), "I'm not a religious woman, Lady. I'm sorry if it pains you, but I believe in no god, and even less do I believe in any church."</i><br><br>*<br><br><i>"How do you expect anyone to believe in your God in these times?"<br><br>"I believe in my God, Majesty."<br><br>"Then you're a fool."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>SHUT UP ALREADY.<br><br>I get it. You don't believe in God, and you think everyone who does is delusional. You don't need to shove it in my face every three seconds (hint: you can also proselytize atheism). <br><br>Just as I get annoyed by extreme moralization and religious undertones imbued in my novels, <b>I also get annoyed by narratives and plot lines that overly proselytize <i>against</i> it</b>.<br><br>The fact is, in this novel, all our cartoon "good guys" did not believe in religion or church, and practically all who did were intolerant or weak or otherwise irrelevant fools.<br>---------------<br><br><br>But getting back to characterization, while I was hoping for this dread-inspiring, almighty evil Red Queen<b>[*]</b>, it was both laughable and disappointing to discover that her greatest, unique trait is being a sexaholic who constantly has sex with her sexy sex slaves.<br><br>That, right there, is pure evil, folks.<br><br>---------------<br><b>[*]</b> Sidenote: Two things come up whenever I hear the term "Red Queen":<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393670507i/8749679.jpg" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393670507i/8749680._SX540_.jpg" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>so that's probably not the imagery <b>Johansen</b> was going for...<br>---------------<br><br><br>However <i>nothing</i> could have sucked more than how Kelsea turned out. <br><br>She was so afraid of turning into her mother that she didn't realize there were far greater crimes than being vain.<br><br>Yeah, her mother liked pretty dresses. So fucking what. <i>I</i> like pretty dresses. <i>I</i> would like to sleep in a comfortable bed. That alone does not make you a bad person and neglectful ruler.<br><br>Kelsea was so terrified of <i>becoming</i> shallow, that she fails to realize that she already <i>is</i> shallow -- and I see now that there is something far worse than being shallow: being shallow and thinking you were profound. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[See what I did there? hurr hurr. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>She is so judgmental of <i>everyone</i> it baffles me. She is spiteful of <i>all</i> her nobles, she doesn't understand that those are the people <i>backing your Kingdom up, fool!</i><br><br>Also, do you know why Eddard Stark died?<br><br>Because he was too honorable and selfless. To be a ruler, you <i>must</i> make sacrifices. You <i>must</i> make hard and abhorrent decisions every now and then, because you <i>must</i> think about the greater good. This does not mean letting your people get wheeled out to the enemy's territories and sold as slaves, but it <i>does</i> mean that, <b>as a ruler, you do not have the luxury to spoil your conscience</b> all the time.<br><br>Kelsea does exactly that, and what frustrates me to no end is that <i>she gets away with it!</i><br><br>In the <i>real</i> Game of Thrones, you would've died a long time ago, Kel.<br><br>So PR people, <i>please</i> stop trying to pass this off as GoT. Nobody's buying it.<br><br>Oh, and also<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393673435ra/8750260.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><i>my review of </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1082980598" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invasion of the Tearling</a>.<br><i>my review of </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1210017247" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fate of the Tearling</a>.<br><br>***<br><i>you can also read more reviews at <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a>.</i><br>***</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1170308258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170308258" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170308258?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170308258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16080094957932655826"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You win your people or you lose your throne.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><b>Fantasy.Adventure.Politics.Plots.War.Magic.Outlaws.Corrupted priests.Betrayal.And a young,plain girl in between.You've gotta love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18712886.The_Queen_of_the_Tearling__The_Queen_of_the_Tearling___1_' title='The Queen of the Tearling (The Queen of the Tearling, #1) by Erika Johansen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of the Tearling</a>!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451429986ra/17540911.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The shipment nears,the cages fill,<br/>A voice rings out across the Tear,<br/>The cages burn,the Keep Lawn still,<br/>The Tearling weeps,the Queen is here.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Kelsea was raised by the Glynns,hiden away from her ambitious uncle and the Red Queen in a desperate effort to keep her alive so th</span>
  <span id="freeText16080094957932655826" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You win your people or you lose your throne.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Fantasy.Adventure.Politics.Plots.War.Magic.Outlaws.Corrupted priests.Betrayal.And a young,plain girl in between.You've gotta love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18712886.The_Queen_of_the_Tearling__The_Queen_of_the_Tearling___1_" title="The Queen of the Tearling (The Queen of the Tearling, #1) by Erika Johansen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of the Tearling</a>!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451429986ra/17540911.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The shipment nears,the cages fill,<br>A voice rings out across the Tear,<br>The cages burn,the Keep Lawn still,<br>The Tearling weeps,the Queen is here.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Kelsea was raised by the Glynns,hiden away from her ambitious uncle and the Red Queen in a desperate effort to keep her alive so that she would claim her throne.Her kingdom was slowly dying,her people were famished,and she didn't even know who her father was and what kind of a queen was her mother.When the time came to rise,she couldn't seperate her friends from her enemies,there were assassins at her steps and no one she could fully rely on but herself and some magical jewels.Thus the reign of the Marked Queen began.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We don't always choose, Majesty. We simply make the best choices we can once the deed is done.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Choices.Choices.Choices.Choose your route,your guards,your servants,your allies.Choose the person you want to be.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6953956.Erika_Johansen" title="Erika Johansen" rel="nofollow noopener">Erika Johansen</a> wrote an <b>extraordinary book</b> about a suffering nation whose only hope was a girl who never left the house she grew up,who was constantly hunted.Her writing is excellent,the narration was in third person yet it gave the reader a better perspective of the heroine,the secondary characters and the villains.I am a huge fan of romance but the lack of it in this book didn't bother me.I do hope though that in the next book there will be more interactions with the mysterious outlaw Fetch (there was a really sexy vibe about him and I think he is my new crush!).Kelsea is a strong and stubborn heroine,willing to sacrifice herself for her people and to right the wrongs her mother committed.There are many questions about the world-building and the Crossing but I am positive they will be answered in the next instalment I'm dying to read it!<b>The story is complex,intriguing and you dive deeply into the world of the Tearling before you even realize it!Great job,Ms.Johansen!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450404158ra/17422648.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1841960872?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1841960872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9574248607001519010">This was a long one and I spent all day today reading it and wow I'm so upset that it's over and if I didn't have such a ridiculous amount of books already I would buy the sequel and read it now. I've seen a lot of people reading the third one so I'm not sure how many people haven't read this one or aren't familiar with it, but the book is about Kelsea who was hidden away as a child for her own safety and is now being taken back to the kingdom to reclaim her thrown. The writing unfolded slowly a</span>
  <span id="freeText9574248607001519010" style="display:none">This was a long one and I spent all day today reading it and wow I'm so upset that it's over and if I didn't have such a ridiculous amount of books already I would buy the sequel and read it now. I've seen a lot of people reading the third one so I'm not sure how many people haven't read this one or aren't familiar with it, but the book is about Kelsea who was hidden away as a child for her own safety and is now being taken back to the kingdom to reclaim her thrown. The writing unfolded slowly and the build was excellent. I appreciate the whole premise of history repeats itself and it's nice to have a female protagonist who's not attractive but is smart and capable. I even started to feel slightly sorry for the Red Queen at the end there. The book left me with so many questions, especially about the whole use of magic and of course about Fetch and Kelsea's father. I would've rated it four stars but even though the ending was adequate it felt kind of less impactful then I was expecting. I was reading the book waiting for the inevitable to happen that everyone keeps freaking out about but then it doesn't happen except we're just given some mysterious bullshit which was interesting and I really want to know how it's going to unfold but still made the ending feel off I guess so four stars not five but it's up there. One of the better fantasy books I've read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9574248607001519010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_904537665" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904537665" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904537665?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18689428-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=apocalypse-post-apocalypse">apocalypse-post-apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=not-your-ordinary-creatures">not-your-ordinary-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904537665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5294243626185768572"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/06/early-review-the-queen-of-the-tearling.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>First and foremost, you need to know that <em>The Queen of the Tearling</em> is NOT a YA Fantasy. As far as I can tell, HarperCollins is not marketing the book that way, but when I read this, "Young Adult" was listed as the second shelf on the Goodreads' genre list (which of course means that Goodreads users are labeling it that way), but it absolutely isn't--Kelsea, the MC, is 19 y.o. and an adult, there is language that at times borders the obscene, and there are circumstances a</span>
  <span id="freeText5294243626185768572" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/06/early-review-the-queen-of-the-tearling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br /><br />First and foremost, you need to know that <em>The Queen of the Tearling</em> is NOT a YA Fantasy. As far as I can tell, HarperCollins is not marketing the book that way, but when I read this, "Young Adult" was listed as the second shelf on the Goodreads' genre list (which of course means that Goodreads users are labeling it that way), but it absolutely isn't--Kelsea, the MC, is 19 y.o. and an adult, there is language that at times borders the obscene, and there are circumstances and (hideous) war stories that have no place in YA literature.<br /><br />I'm kind of at a loss with what to do with this book.<br /><br />On the one hand . . . I really (REALLY) liked it. On the other hand . . . there are problems that absolutely cannot be ignored.<br /><br />I think it's time for another list.<br /><br /><strong>What I liked about <em>The Queen of the Tearling</em>:</strong><br /><br />1. It held my attention despite the numerous problems. It <em>more</em> than held my attention; I couldn't put it down. I read ALL OF IT in less than 12 hours (and this was not a short book). Maybe in less than 10 hours. Should've timed it . . .<br /><br />2. Kelsea is not perfect. She's a typical 19 y.o. girl with all of the inherit insecurities and inexperience. She's not exceptionally beautiful or talented, she's just a girl who loves history and books who happenes to be born royal.<br /><br />3. Lots of important social and political messages.<br /><br />4. New and mind-blowing world-building premise:<br /><br />So check this out---something (we don't know what) happened (we don't know when) and the Americans and the British left (for parts unknown) on ships to rebuild civilization. And life has reverted back to the Medieval period. But with MAGIC, so it's like a real world fantasy. Pretty cool, I think.<br /><br /><strong>What I didn't like about <em>The Queen of the Tearling</em>:</strong><br /><br />1. We don't know what, we don't know when, we don't know where.<br /><br />2. And this is the real problem . . . There are so many similarities between this book and other books I've read that I'm not entirely convinced that the new and mind-blowing world-building premise is really new and mind-blowing, and not just from some other book I have yet to read.<br /><br />Sound harsh?<br /><br />Well, there are unignorable similarities between this book and no less than THREE other book series/movies that I have read/seen, and a strong argument can be put forth for a . . . fourth. (&lt;------can things like that happen in any other language besides English?)<br /> <br />	 <strong>The <em>Wheel of Time</em> by Robert Jordan</strong>---a "Tearling" is a person from Tear, which is also the name of one of the world powers in WoT, Almont Plain is a mere one letter away from being the Almoth Plain, which lies between the WoT's Arad Doman and Tarabon, and Kelsea is a young and somewhat sheltered royal with a fascination, but not much understanding, for the curses that men much more readily use (in her world), very much like a certain royal in the WoT (Elayne Trakand, the Daughter-Heir of Andor). <br /><br />	 <strong>The <em>Fire and Thorns</em> Trilogy by Rae Carson</strong>---if I were to try to enumerate everything that <em>The Queen of the Tearling</em> has in common with this trilogy, there would be room for nothing else. Kelsea is in possession of interlocking blue stones that give her prophetic dreams, guide her both physically and mentally, and instill her with magical power of some kind. There is a huge emphasis on religion (this time as a manipulative political machine). The adult charged with protecting Kelsea underestimates and undermines her, and is thus nearly sent away from her (male instead of female). Kelsea is overweight and unattractive, rather than the typical and beautiful princess-type, etc. Like I said, I could go for days. <br /><br />	 <strong><em>V for Vendetta</em></strong>---The IMDB synopsis for this movie is, <em>"In a future British tyranny, a shadowy freedom fighter plots to overthrow it with the help of a young woman."</em> The Fetch is a shadowy (harlequin mask-wearing) freedom fighter who plots to overthrow TWO governments with the help of a young QUEEN whom he manipulatively tests to ascertain her true feelings/intentions. Just. Like. V. <br /> <br />So no matter how entertained I was by this book---and how could I not be? It's seemingly based on two of my favorite book series and one of my favorite movies---I can't in good conscience rate it highly.<br /><br />But will I continue with the series? I honestly don't know. There was an interesting development in the last 10(ish)% of the book that I'm curious to see where the author is going with, and I have this morbid curiosity (almost <em>schadenfreude</em>) to see if the pattern continues . . . but does the curiosity outweigh the incredulity at these blatant similarities? I guess we'll see . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="5294243626185768572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_887053569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/887053569" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/887053569?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=2-star-reads">2-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer887053569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17937367923870053819"><b>Don’t you just hate book labels?</b><br/><br/>Many other reviews seem to centre on the point that this is labelled as a cross between <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>A Game of Thrones.</i> I’m just absolutely sick of hearing such things. Anybody who has read more than ten pages of either will realise the statement is completely untrue. It’s quite an annoying comparison. Certainly, you could say it’s like The Hunger Games insomuch that it has a female character as the protagonist. Such a parallel isn’t it? And I suppose you </span>
  <span id="freeText17937367923870053819" style="display:none"><b>Don’t you just hate book labels?</b><br /><br />Many other reviews seem to centre on the point that this is labelled as a cross between <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>A Game of Thrones.</i> I’m just absolutely sick of hearing such things. Anybody who has read more than ten pages of either will realise the statement is completely untrue. It’s quite an annoying comparison. Certainly, you could say it’s like The Hunger Games insomuch that it has a female character as the protagonist. Such a parallel isn’t it? And I suppose you could say it’s like A Game of Thrones because people squabble over a throne. Again, it’s such a unique parallel that is rarely ever seen in fantasy…….<br /><br />These sorts of labels seem to only be getting worse. Whenever I look in a bookshop and go to the fantasy section I’ll see a sign saying something like “because you like <i>A Game of Thrones.”</i> And then there will be a load of books next to it that are nothing like the series, clearly placed there by some random moron who saw a sword on the cover. I’ve even seen the same suggestions on historical fiction. On the back of one of Bernard Cornwell’s books here in the UK it says <i>“like A Game of Thrones</i> but real”. How annoying. I love <i> A Song of Ice and Fire </i> as much as the next fantasy geek, probably more so, but trying to relate every book to it is just fucking frustrating. It’s becoming such an overused comparison.<br /> <br />So many reviews seem to have let that affect their rating of this book; it appears to me that this initial feeling has distorted their opinions of the novel. I believe this to be very unfair: this label has affected people’s feelings toward something that should be read without considering what the misleading PR says about it. It’s a common case of a judging a book by its cover. So a quick word of advice, completely ignore the comparisons because you may not enjoy the book. Your initial expectations will fall flat. I’ll be honest this is a rather average book, so if you expect a cultural phenomenon you’ll be drastically disappointed rather than marginally so. <br /><br />I’ll endeavour to review this book for what it is: an original fantasy novel that has no major comparisons, whatsoever, with the afore mentioned books. But, that doesn’t necessarily mean that it’s good. <br /><br />Kelsea is the heir to the kingdom of Tearling, a kingdom in which her corrupt Uncle has claimed the regency. In this coming of age story she must, with the help of her mother’s former guard, take her thrown. The men serving her are not bound to her out of blind faith to her blood, but to her supposed worthiness as a ruler. Mace, the captain of her guard is the embodiment of this. He took his time to know her before granting her his trust. His loyalty wasn’t cheap. Why waste your life following a moron? <br /><br />As the story progresses her power grows as a ruler; her grasp on her mysterious magical power strengthens along with her confidence. She undergoes a great deal of character development and still has room for much more in later books. Accompanying this is an interesting collection of side characters, which each have their own issues to deal with; there are themes of redemption, treachery and tyrannical ruling that haunts their footsteps. The plot is told in an energetic manner, but it is rather trite. I mean, we’ve all read this kind of thing before a dozen times already. The romance was rather obvious as was the direction this will take in the future. So there are a few issues. <br /><br />The author has made the same mistake that Mark Lawrence did with his broken empire trilogy. She’s made a medieval type fantasy universe, but only after the destruction of what I can only presume is modern day. I hate this idea. We’re reading fantasy, but then we have a reference to the American slave trade or another one to European technological advances and even genetics. It ruins the feel of the setting. It made this feel like a book that didn’t quite know what it wanted to be. If you want to write about that, do a sci-fi novel. I like my fantasy books to be fantasy books. I hate hybrids. And because of this I will not be reading any further. It turned into one big mess in which those original labels just looked laughable. I mean they made no sense. But, that’s beside the point. This was rather average anyway. It’s not terrible, but it just hasn’t got a lot going for it. I wouldn’t recommend it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17937367923870053819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
