<div id="review_2288497815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288497815" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288497815?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288497815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13859210294070795826">I decided to read this on a whim even though I had no idea what it was about, and I really loved it!!!! <br/><br/><i> The mark of a true hero is that the most heroic of his deeds is done in secret. We never hear of it. And yet somehow, my friends, we know </i><br/><br/><b> What I liked </b><br/><br/>- Although this isn’t high fantasy, it read like a high fantasy book, and I think that is why some people found it boring. It was mostly planning and plotting but I never found it boring for some reason. There were also some action parts thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText13859210294070795826" style="display:none">I decided to read this on a whim even though I had no idea what it was about, and I really loved it!!!! <br /><br /><i> The mark of a true hero is that the most heroic of his deeds is done in secret. We never hear of it. And yet somehow, my friends, we know </i><br /><br /><b> What I liked </b><br /><br />- Although this isn’t high fantasy, it read like a high fantasy book, and I think that is why some people found it boring. It was mostly planning and plotting but I never found it boring for some reason. There were also some action parts though which I loved. If you don’t like high fantasy books then you might not enjoy this<br /><br />- I loved the side characters especially the charming Fetch. I wish he was in this more<br /><br />- This book has multiple POVs and I enjoyed each one which is a rare occurrence. I loved how every POV was relevant and interesting and not used in a filler way. <br /><br />- I found the plot and world unique: they live in the future that looks like the past. When you think of the future, you think of technological advancement and stuff, and not back to horses, castles and the old world, so that was interesting. Although I found the history kinda confusing and I don’t think I understand what really happened (was it even explained? I’m not sure lol)<br /><br /><b> Some notes </b><br />- I don’t think this is a YA book. In fact, the MC is the only teenager in this book and the majority of the characters are over 30. Plus there is a lot of subject matters such as rape, paedophilia, child killings and strong languages that seemed more adult than YA.<br /><br />- This book has LONG chapters. They were only 14 chapters and the book is almost 450 pages long<br /><br />- There isn’t romance in this. The MC had a crush on someone but that was basically it but I still enjoyed the book regardless of this fact (I make mention of this because I kinda don’t like reading books with no romance)<br /><br />- I try to avoid mainstream books with Christianity in them because they are usually portrayed in a bad light and in this, the ‘church’ is mostly portrayed in a bad/hypocritical way. Fortunately, there is an important side character that is a priest and also a good person. <br /><br />Overall, it was an interesting book and I found myself hooked from the beginning to the end. Although I am still indecisive about whether I like the MC or not. At this point, I’m mostly neutral.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13859210294070795826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1307573870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307573870" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307573870?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062328090" href="/book/show/18698884-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307573870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17322945281201982011">After 6 months, I've finally found a novel worthy of 5 stars. It took me that long to finally get out of the dreaded reading slump. It should've been obvious though, because one of the options to get out of the slump is to go back to your roots. My roots being Fantasy. I shouldn't have looked elsewhere.<br/><br/>There is a bit of a story when it comes to why I bought and eventually read this novel. Let me try to keep things short though so that I can jump in to the review. <br/><br/>I was having a normal day, brows</span>
  <span id="freeText17322945281201982011" style="display:none">After 6 months, I've finally found a novel worthy of 5 stars. It took me that long to finally get out of the dreaded reading slump. It should've been obvious though, because one of the options to get out of the slump is to go back to your roots. My roots being Fantasy. I shouldn't have looked elsewhere.<br /><br />There is a bit of a story when it comes to why I bought and eventually read this novel. Let me try to keep things short though so that I can jump in to the review. <br /><br />I was having a normal day, browsing through Goodreads, when I first stumbled upon this novel. A friend of mine wrote a review of it, giving it a 1-star rating. Every time one of my friends gives a 1-star rating, I instantly read the review and view the summary of the novel. It's always intriguing as to why a person hated a novel so much. Some of my friends were enraged because people were comparing this to Game of Thrones and The Hunger Games. I myself hate those novel comparisons, unless they're spot-on in terms of similarities. I considered their reviews, I stayed away from this, but every time I visited my local bookstore the novel was always on the featured shelf. It was tempting, so I read the description on the back. I liked what I read, but the negative reviews creeped back in my mind, and I decided to put the book back on the shelf. This went on for months, but eventually I gave in. I bought the book, and it was the best decision I've ever made.<br /><br />Kelsea Raleigh has been hiding her whole life, but on her nineteenth birthday, it was finally her time to claim her rightful place as The Queen of the Tearling. Her journey will not be easy, as there are aspiring people who wants nothing but to see her dead. Her uncle and The Red Queen wants her dead the most. She will need to learn to become a queen, and it's as complicated as it sounds. Being a queen is not merely ruling the people who is in her command, but rather it's about making the right decisions, sacrifice, combat, politics, tactics, having to deal with an absurd amount of betrayals, to name a few.<br /><br />I'm always up for an epic adventure, and the Fantasy genre is most of the time fulfilling of that yearning. Aside from a good plot, the characters in a fantasy novel must not only be interesting, but also fully-developed in the end. I can consider Kelsea as a character who fully-developed in the end of this first novel. She is a coward in the beginning of the novel, but as the novel goes on, she learns what it truly means to become a queen, or rather, a True Queen. I like reading about characters who are weak in the beginning, but ends up becoming powerful in the end, but written proficiently. What I mean is, don't force your character to develop just for the sake of presenting a "powerful" character in the end, because it will always turn out bad. The author managed to create a genuine powerful character in this novel. It took her the whole novel to fully develop Kelsea, and that's how things should be. <br /><br />Supporting characters are just as important in fantasy novels, and Mace (Lazarus) is probably one of the best characters written. I liked his role in the novel. He wasn't dull in any aspect, and he helped the character of Kelsea to develop. Mace is a man of mystery, there is nothing much to say about him, but he did some amazing things for the queen. I'm hoping to read more about him in the next novel.<br /><br />The Red Queen is the main villain in this novel. I liked the way the author wrote her character. She appears malevolent in front of the crowd, but she has dark secrets of her own, and no one knows about them. She's not this perfect villain who is so powerful that the character ends up becoming corny in the end. She has her flaws, and it's a joyride to read about her struggles. It's quite obvious that she will have a huge role in the next novel, I'm just hoping she made the right choice.<br /><br />The plot has a lot of plot twists and interesting events. I'm honestly not sure why this is considered as Young-Adult, but it's more of Adult-Fantasy for me. The novel contains graphic violence, profanity, and other things that young-adults seem to hate. I get it, you didn't ask for a gritty and inhumane novel, but it wasn't written for your age anyway. Another thing, if the author wrote an inhumane novel, it doesn't necessarily mean that they are inhumane in nature. It will almost all the time be for the plot and character development.<br /><br />I really enjoyed everything that happened in the novel. I liked her decisions, and also the Mace's. Every decision they made contributed to the story development. I don't want to spoil anything, but you will understand what I'm talking about if you read this.<br /><br />Another thing, I really wanted the characters I was rooting for to have their way. Just like in George RR Martin's A Song of Ice and Fire series, I was rooting for certain characters to live, and also certain characters to die. It was no different for A Queen of Tearling. There were a few who I wanted to succeed, and also a few who I wanted to fail and be tormented. It's always important to have strong characters, and this novel has that.<br /><br />I respectfully agree with the 1-star review of my friends. I understand why they hated this novel so much. It's just that I didn't see their problems as problems of my own, and I don't see what's wrong with that. People have different opinions, and different novels will cater to the needs of different people. I do have a lot of similar opinions with them though in other novels, but this time it just didn't match. I'm not going to bash their review, just like I'm sure they won't bash mine. It's almost 2016 people, learn to respect the opinion of other people.<br /><br />5/5 stars. One of the best reads I've had for 2015. It's always the unexpected ones that make a huge impact on me. I can't wait to read the sequel. I bought the sequel when I was only 50 pages in with this one, but I knew greatness awaits. I'm really hoping the second novel would be just as good as this, if not better.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17322945281201982011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839273685?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593072691" href="/book/show/17415882-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=print-arc">print-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=can-t-believe-i-finished">can-t-believe-i-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=no-just-no">no-just-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=poor-world-building">poor-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=youve-got-to-be-kidding-me">youve-got-to-be-kidding-me</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839273685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3728619293727593453">Well, this was terrible. I hated everything but the cover.<br/><br/>I’m proud of myself for finishing this <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> even though it’s turned out to be one of my most disappointing reads this year. HarperCollins was really pushing this title marking-wise, and while it’s not considered YA, they did offer it to quite a few YA bloggers for consideration for review. I had to be the special person to request it. I wish I hadn’t have done that.<br/><br/><i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> tried to do a lot of things</span>
  <span id="freeText3728619293727593453" style="display:none">Well, this was terrible. I hated everything but the cover.<br /><br />I’m proud of myself for finishing this <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> even though it’s turned out to be one of my most disappointing reads this year. HarperCollins was really pushing this title marking-wise, and while it’s not considered YA, they did offer it to quite a few YA bloggers for consideration for review. I had to be the special person to request it. I wish I hadn’t have done that.<br /><br /><i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> tried to do a lot of things and that’s its biggest problem. You can’t have a high fantasy, historic society set in the future and NOT do any type of world building. You can’t have set rules up in your world only to break it because MAGIC. It’s not nice to tease the reader from the very beginning of SECRETS and have you supporting cast dangle it in from of us like a carrot for the entirety of the novel and NEVER TELL US by the end. Because that’s exactly what happened. It really made me question what the point of the novel was considering I learned nothing new about the plot or characters by the end.<br /><br />I’m also surprised this was marketed as Adult to YA readers when it really is just a poorly plotted MG fantasy. For all this book had going for it — and it had a lot, including a movie deal with Emma Watson attached to star! — I expected so much more. I expected to be blown away, and maybe that was part of the problem, but really the level of SUCK contained in <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> is baffling. I don’t recommend it at all.</span>

<div id="review_1288846471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288846471" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288846471?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=makes-me-want-to-puke">makes-me-want-to-puke</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=das-ungeheuer-is-to-blame">das-ungeheuer-is-to-blame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=tstl-characters">tstl-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=lost-faith-in-humanity">lost-faith-in-humanity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288846471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9232059421999099271"><b>Ladies and gentlemen, I'm warning you: This is a rage rant.</b><br/><br/>Let me present you the future:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437107020i/15539058._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>No, really. That's the future according to this book – I'm not shitting you. Our future is a freaking Medieval town.<br/><br/>Kelsea was raised alone with two guardians. She believes herself plain and ugly and totally unimportant. Tunrs out she's a special snowflake: She's the long-lost heir of the Tearling. Now she's the queen and she's getting back to “civilization.” (haha, what civilization?)<br/><br/>The synopsis didn't cat</span>
  <span id="freeText9232059421999099271" style="display:none"><b>Ladies and gentlemen, I'm warning you: This is a rage rant.</b><br><br>Let me present you the future:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437107020i/15539058._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, really. That's the future according to this book – I'm not shitting you. Our future is a freaking Medieval town.<br><br>Kelsea was raised alone with two guardians. She believes herself plain and ugly and totally unimportant. Tunrs out she's a special snowflake: She's the long-lost heir of the Tearling. Now she's the queen and she's getting back to “civilization.” (haha, what civilization?)<br><br>The synopsis didn't catch my attention. In fact, I started this book dubious – it has polarizing reviews and I tended to agree the most with the negative ones. However, reviews from the same people that rated this 1 star had been giving high ratings to the second book, so of course I had to see for myself if this was as bad as it was painted to be.<br><br>Turns out I was wrong: It was worse.<br><br>First of all, the most important thing in a fantasy novel is the world-building. Where was it in this book? I know not. As I said in the beginning, this is supposedly set in the future, but the future here is Medieval – people use horses as transportation, swords and maces to fight, etc.<br><br>I was asking myself all the time how in hell would people abandon all the commodities we have now to go back centuries ahead to an era in which I would absolutely hate living. Really? WHY WOULD THEY STOP USING ELECTRICITY? WHY WOULD PEOPLE START USING HORSES AGAIN INSTEAD OF CARS? Makes no sense, and it's not explained.<br><br>The kingdom is not explained either. All we know is that there's a queen. Yeah. There's a queen, and so what? I want to know more about the politics! How do they organise themselves in here?<br><br>That's all I'm going to say about the world, because this is where the real rage starts: I. Freaking. Hated. Kelsea.<br><br>Kelsea is the famous queen of the <s>Mary Sues</s> Tearling. She's very childish and annoying. When she gets to the Tearling, she starts throwing orders at everyone like a sulky 2-year-old would do just because she's the queen.<br><br><blockquote>“I am the Queen of the Tearling! Open the cages!”</blockquote><br><br>That is an actual quote from the book. If that doesn't prove the fat she's acting like a 2-year-old and not like the 19-year-old she's supposed to be, then <i>this</i> should show it:<br><br><blockquote>“All of you down there! You’re part of <i>my</i> government, and <i>my</i> army! You will open the cages!”</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437107086ra/15539064.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bahahahahahahhahahahhahaha. You sure know how stupid you sound, don't you, Kelsea?<br><br>But Kelsea's greatest treat is that she's a Mary Sue.<br><br><blockquote>She’d always been thick, but now she’d been indoors too long, and between that and her injuries, whatever physical condition she might have had was gone. No queen in a storybook ever had to deal with such a problem.</blockquote><br><br>How's that for a Mary Sue?<br><br>Or no, actually no. Now that I remember, her best treat is that she diminishes everyone else so she can feel superior. Case in point:<br><br><blockquote>He was the ugliest creature Kelsea had ever seen in her life.<br><br><i>Finally,</i> she thought, regretting her own unkindness even as it crossed her mind, <i>someone who makes me look beautiful.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>First, that is perhaps the most mary-sue-ish comment I've read in my whole life. Second... what the hell is wrong <i>with</i> you, Kelsea? You don't do that to people! It's just <i>wrong</i>. That is not enough for her, though. Later, she says this:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>What does she see when she looks in the mirror?</i> Kelsea wondered. How could a woman who looked so old still place so much importance on being attractive? She had read about this particular delusion in books many times, but it was different to see it in practice. And for all the anguish that Kelsea’s own reflection had caused her lately, she saw now that there was something far worse than being ugly: being ugly and thinking you were beautiful.</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436057734ra/15413776.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jesus Christ, there are many teenagers who suffer because they have low self-esteem. Now imagine how their lives would be if Kelsea was present in them. Just... no. You don't insult others just to make yourself look better: It's coward.<br><br>Also, this:<br><br><blockquote>“I can’t speak to political salvation, Majesty. I’m a spiritual adviser.”<br><br>“No one needs spiritual advice right now.”<br><br>Tyler spoke more sharply than he intended. “Those who cease to worry about their souls often find them difficult to reclaim later, Majesty. God doesn’t make such distinctions.”<br><br>“How do you expect anyone to believe in your God in these times?”<br><br>“I believe in my God, Majesty.”<br><br>“Then you’re a fool.”<br><br>Tyler straightened and spoke coldly. “You’re welcome to believe what you like, and think what you like of my church, but don’t malign my faith. Not in front of me.”</blockquote><br><br>I've got to say: I don't believe in god, but I respect people who do. I have absolutely no problem with religious people. In fact, I used to be like that. I would <i>never</i> say remarks like that. It's disrespectful and narrow-minded.<br><br>Now, throw in some sexist comments and you have ta da! The Queen of the Tearling!<br><br><blockquote>
<i>Women scream when they’re hurt,</i> Barty’s voice echoed in her head. <i>Men scream when they’re dying.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Plus, it was boring. B-O-R-I-N-G. Not because of the pacing (there was no pace), but because every single thing that happened was zero interesting. EVERYTHING WAS BORING.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404406107ra/10234221.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So yeah, I regret reading this. I never expected it to be as atrocious as it was. I will probably read the sequel, but just because that was the reason why I initially read this. I apologize if my review is a mess, but my head is a mess right now and I'm just hoping I can recover from this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9232059421999099271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1618435329" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618435329" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618435329?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40229477-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=gurrrl-power">gurrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=alternate-reality-or-history">alternate-reality-or-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=your-argument-is-invalid">your-argument-is-invalid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-dystopian">fantasy-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=this-book-is-everything">this-book-is-everything</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618435329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer188775085068308381">$1.99 on US Kindle: February 6, 2020<br/><br/><b>First things first, <u>more Fetch please</u>.</b><br/><br/>Here we have a book that dares to cross genres. It’s a fantasy/dystopian blend that is mostly-vague about the origin details. We know there was a world very similar to ours, same country names, technology, books, and culture. Then, “something happened” in an event known as The Crossing and we lost technology, electricity, advanced medicine, and were reduced to living in a world with torches, swords, archery, farming, hunti</span>
  <span id="freeText188775085068308381" style="display:none">$1.99 on US Kindle: February 6, 2020<br /><br /><b>First things first, <u>more Fetch please</u>.</b><br /><br />Here we have a book that dares to cross genres. It’s a fantasy/dystopian blend that is mostly-vague about the origin details. We know there was a world very similar to ours, same country names, technology, books, and culture. Then, “something happened” in an event known as The Crossing and we lost technology, electricity, advanced medicine, and were reduced to living in a world with torches, swords, archery, farming, hunting, villagers and nobles, etc. etc. <br /><br />This is the story of a 19-year-old girl who is the heir to the Tearling throne, had been hidden and raised by foster parents until she came of age, and then has to suddenly become a queen. Her kingdom has been brutalized by her uncle, who was Regent, and by a neighboring evil queen who demands a repulsive monthly tithe of Tear slaves.<br /><br />Kelsea is the new, young queen and she immediately begins making changes and struggles to earn the respect of her guards and citizens. This was a book that ended without a cliffhanger, but there were plenty of pieces that are still to be resolved.<br /><br />What I really liked:<br /><br />-	Kelsea was great. She is one of my new favorite female characters. She is no Mary Sue and has to fight and earn her place. She is assertive and confident and yet still has the realistic self-doubt of any young woman concerning her looks and desirability. I thought there was a lot of girl power in this!<br />-	As I mentioned, no cliffhanger. The first part of the story ends satisfactorily, but makes you want more because there are still at least two people that Kelsea will potentially have an epic showdown with.<br />-	No romantic angst or manufactured drama! (There is no romance in this at all, actually.)<br /><br />The only minor issue I had was that the book felt a bit over-long, but the pacing was still pretty even. <br /><br />I would not classify this as Young Adult. There was no smut, but there were graphic descriptions of sex, rape, and abuse to women and children. People got their throats cut and were gutted. The main character is 19 when the story starts and everyone else is older than her, so if anything, it’s “New Adult.”<br /><br />I enjoyed this enough that I am putting it on my favorites shelf and would buy a physical copy and re-read it at some point.<br /><br />Buddy read with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo group</a>.<br /><br />This book has some very mixed reviews and I have addressed some of those points below.<br /><br /><br /><br />I'm going to start writing some things out here in response to some reviews I've been reading, which I happen to disagree with. We all have different experiences of course, but these are my responses to a few issues some readers had.<br /><br />1) <u>The dystopian/medieval hybrid world.</u> Who says someone can't merge genres and why is an author required to explain every single thing about the world in the first book (or at all)? Fantasy that has castles, swords, and royal courts don't have to be strictly "high/epic" fantasy. The author chose to merge our world with an alternate history/future. I don't get why this makes some people angry. If we lost technology and modern medicine and gasoline and the electrical grid, etc. etc. etc., who says we couldn't (or wouldn't) revert back to a civilization like this? *genuinely baffled why this is an issue*<br /><br />2) <u>Kelsea.</u> She has only lived with two older adults her whole life and then, when suddenly around a bunch of men, notices they are attractive. *shock* Why wouldn't a 19 year old woman see the men around her as being people she is (or isn't) attracted to? Why is it a big deal if she thinks herself plain and has issue with her appearance? I sure did when I was 19. Whether right or wrong, I looked at other women and compared myself sometimes. Why can't a character be genuinely "plain" and notice she is "average" without it being proof she has low self-esteem? I personally find Kelsea a strong female character. *scratching head*<br /><br />3)<u> Her guards.</u> Apparently, because they talk at night and drink and are rowdy, they are sucky guards and unrealistic. I also disagree with this because they had no one worthy of guarding and morale was low. They became undisciplined and life has just not been good to anyone in the Tearling kingdom. The Regent is horrible, the tyrannical Queen who rules in the neighboring kingdom has sucked the joy out of life. At this point, they are more like a roguish group of guys who stayed together because it was all they knew. But they snap out of it quickly once they see Kelsea is worthy of their time and loyalty. Not sure why this is an issue either. <br /><br /><b>First post:</b><br /><b>17 MAY 2016: $1.99 on Kindle</b><br /><br />This has some crazy mixed reviews, but I still want to try it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="188775085068308381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14562008949612404067"><b>Edit : 25/12/2017 : I have a copy of the second book but I have no interest in reading it. So I'll just abandon it. </b><br/><br/><s>
  <b>3.5 Stars</b>
</s><b> rounded down to 3 Stars</b><br/><br/>When Kelsea Raleigh was a baby, She was smuggled out from the palace for her own safety and since then she was fostered by two servants who pledged their lives to raise her and protect her until she claimed her throne.<br/>when she was 3 year old her mother, Queen Elyssa Raleigh died and Kelsea's uncle, Thomas Raleigh was in charge since then.<br/>sixteen</span>
  <span id="freeText14562008949612404067" style="display:none"><b>Edit : 25/12/2017 : I have a copy of the second book but I have no interest in reading it. So I'll just abandon it. </b><br><br><s>
  <b>3.5 Stars</b>
</s><b> rounded down to 3 Stars</b><br><br>When Kelsea Raleigh was a baby, She was smuggled out from the palace for her own safety and since then she was fostered by two servants who pledged their lives to raise her and protect her until she claimed her throne.<br>when she was 3 year old her mother, Queen Elyssa Raleigh died and Kelsea's uncle, Thomas Raleigh was in charge since then.<br>sixteen years later, on Kelsea's nineteenth birthday, The queen's guard came to her cottage, where she was raised in hiding to escort her to the palace to be the Queen of the tearling. <br><br><u>
  <b>My Opinion</b>
</u> <br><br>when I saw this book in a bookstore, I was immediately stunned by the gorgeous cover. I heard this book was great it but I also heard this book was bad. I didn't really intend on buying this book but I still don't know what possessed me because when I came out the bookstore I already had this book among the other books I bought. <br>I was fooled by the cover, I thought the story would be awesome. I had a very high expectation on this book, I knew there isn't any romance in this book but I didn't care about it as long as story was great. but the story was SOOO slow and wasn't that great so this was what happened to me while reading it<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386214990ra/7313753.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was torn between stop reading it or keep reading it. But I chose to keep reading it because I already bought the second book and I didn't want to waste my money. <br>But I have to admit that the beginning of the story was pretty good but I got bored reading it when I reached the middle of this book and the MC annoyed me. I'm going to tell you which part she annoyed me so much. <br><br> <i>Venner put his sword back in its scabbard, his face disgruntled. <br>" Only three days till you can torment me further, arms master." <br>" I torment you for your own good, Lady"</i><br><br>seriously, I was so mad when she said that to him because she asked the arms master to teach her about sword fighting and then she got what she wanted but she acted like that!?!?! what the hell did she want?!?!?! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397291ra/766436.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why Did I Give This Book 3 Stars ? <br><br>I gave this book 3 stars because it's original, this book made me laughing twice and I like The Fetch. The Fetch always made me giggling ❤❤❤ I kept reading this book just because of this guy. oh and I need to tell you guys about this <br><br><i>he took Kelsea's chin in one hand, spearing her with his black gaze. " should you ever gain the throne in truth, I expect to see your policies implemented. They're much in need of refinement, and likely doomed to failure in execution, but they're good policies, and the show an understanding of political history that most monarchs never take the trouble to achieve. You'll rule by the principles you've outlined, and you'll attempt to cure the blight on this land, no matter what it costs you. This is <i>my</i> test, and if you fail, you will answer to me. <br><br>Kelsea raised her eyebrows, trying to hide the shiver that passed through her. "you think you could get to me once I'm in the Keep?"<br>"I can get to anyone in this kingdom. I am more dangerous than the Mort, more dangerous than the Caden. I've stolen many things from the Regent, snd he's been under my knife. I could've killed him many times over, but that I had to wait."<br>"for what?" <br>"for you, Tear Queen."<br>Then he was up and gone from the table in one fluid motion, and Kelsea was left staring after him, her face burning where his fingers had been. </i> <br><br>the moment he treatened Kelsea, that was the moment I fell in love with him, am I weird guys? xD<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394940262ra/8927063.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Will I read the second book ?<br><br>if I hadn't bought the second book, I would not have read the sequel but I already bought the sequel, So I think I have to read it and the reason I read the sequel is because of The Fetch. hehehe. I need to know more about him. <br><br>Thank you so much for reading my review about this book guys!! <br>Happy Reading to all of you!! ❤❤❤</span>

<div id="review_1638198988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638198988?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohammed Arabey" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638198988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8792556856842160664">I, as Emma Watson also said, <i>devoured it in less than a week, couldn’t put the bloody thing down..</i>,<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081787i/22184076._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='210' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I wanted to end it, yet for me, for a different reason.<br/>Like her, <i>I couldn't hate it</i>, but can't love it either..<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081787i/22184077._SX540_.jpg' width='449' height='336' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>They called it <b>"Feminist Alternative To 'Game Of Thrones'"</b>!!<br/>Come on, it's a "Mini-Game of A Throne" full of feminism, Rant, and even out-cursed GOT.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081932i/22184086._SX540_.png' width='450' height='260' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u><br/>The Story<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463511895i/19127058._SY540_.jpg' width='380' height='599' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></u>
  </b>
</blockquote>A Queen is back when she's turned 19...She must claim her Throne from her evil Uncle/Regent..<br/>She must look for her Kingdo</span>
  <span id="freeText8792556856842160664" style="display:none">I, as Emma Watson also said, <i>devoured it in less than a week, couldn’t put the bloody thing down..</i>,<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081787i/22184076._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I wanted to end it, yet for me, for a different reason.<br>Like her, <i>I couldn't hate it</i>, but can't love it either..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081787i/22184077._SX540_.jpg" width="449" height="336" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>They called it <b>"Feminist Alternative To 'Game Of Thrones'"</b>!!<br>Come on, it's a "Mini-Game of A Throne" full of feminism, Rant, and even out-cursed GOT.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081932i/22184086._SX540_.png" width="450" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u><br>The Story<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463511895i/19127058._SY540_.jpg" width="380" height="599" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></u>
  </b>
</blockquote>A Queen is back when she's turned 19...She must claim her Throne from her evil Uncle/Regent..<br>She must look for her Kingdom, The Tearling.. must defend it against the evil neighbor, Red Queen..<br>.<br>.<br>Yep, that's all, I guess.<br><br>Oh, and she also must learn about her mother's, the previous Queen past..But that's not the mystery here...<br>The Mystery is the fuss Emma Watson making about the novel..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463511895i/19127059._SY540_.png" width="430" height="638" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I mean, everything bugs me in a YA is doubled here..<br>A Tiresome pace, Unimaginable world history!!, Too much Unnecessary Characters Describing and inner thoughts..<br>And RANT, lots and lots of rants in every topic forced in every minor related event.<br>AND swears , yeah it's so much of it that I forget it's a YA anyway.<br>She out cursed GOT, seriously in less than half the pages of Game of Thrones, she said 'fuck, shit, bitch, cock, cunt, etc" about 90% more of book one of Game of Thrones..<br><br>Well..<br>at least the rest of what I hate of YA isn't here anyway.. The silly Love Triangle Story.. there's even No love story here, imagine? FEMINISM baby!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>The Setting</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489087545i/22184714._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="241" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>In a Futuristic Medieval Europe !!!!</b><br>-second time after Red Queen.. the worst mash up EVER in the history of literature.-<br>Apparently USA blown up and people crossed the ocean to ‘New Europe’ whatever happens to told one? We don't know yet.<br>Apparently they forget the everything.... even guns!!<i> so it was a shocking moment when the Mort “neighbors of Tearling” re-discovered Gunpowder.</i><br><br>They are divided into Mort and Tear.. 2 Kingdoms where Morris Queen -The Red Queen- want to take over Tearling.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>The Characters</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489081787i/22184076._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Kelsea Raleigh Glynn's 19 , so not much of age issue here as most YA- some queens are 16 only-.. and she's a bit good character as well.. strong and tough, <b>AND PLAIN</b> , remember, Plain, must be said many times, since Plain is the new Beautiful ..FEMINISM baby!<br>and the good thing is that, she loves books.<br><i>-she has this set of 7 books of Harry Potter, that's funny disturbing the mood of the whole Kingdom thing, I mean they don't have Guns anymore, but they have Harry Potter, but I can't say no for a Queen who loves Harry Potter-</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462476833i/19002927._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="325" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't feel anything to the rest of the characters save Lazarus “will be played by Russell Crow I guess” who's loyal and reminded me with old Jorah Mormont of GOT.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489087545i/22184715._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="241" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Red Queen is so typical Old Disney witch evil queen types… but with R rate “she does sex as Cersei, yet she's not even 1% as deep character as her”<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461468131i/18870843._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="241" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Finally</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It Was Ok.. 2 stars are so enough..<br>just another YA novel..<br>Not A Game of Thrones at all... just a small kingdom throne between 2 queens.. "Queens fight is coming :)" <br><br>Anyway, I hope it'd get better in the next book.. cause, I bought the first two together :(<br><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>Read from 14 May 2016<br>To 20 May 2016</span>
  <a data-text-id="8792556856842160664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1331775763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1331775763" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1331775763?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857502476" href="/book/show/23482780-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1331775763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14622522881192423917"><b>"We don't always choose, Majesty. We simply make the best choices we can once the deed is done."</b><br/><br/>•I'll start with the bad because yes, I am that obnoxious. The book is set in this kingdom, the Tearling, which, along with other kingdoms and empires, was born and grew on a previously unknown land after the so-called Crossing. We are told very little about this event: we only know, basically, that said Crossing was made by the Americans, and that some bits of the late America's culture still last. M</span>
  <span id="freeText14622522881192423917" style="display:none"><b>"We don't always choose, Majesty. We simply make the best choices we can once the deed is done."</b><br /><br />•I'll start with the bad because yes, I am that obnoxious. The book is set in this kingdom, the Tearling, which, along with other kingdoms and empires, was born and grew on a previously unknown land after the so-called Crossing. We are told very little about this event: we only know, basically, that said Crossing was made by the Americans, and that some bits of the late America's culture still last. My problem is, <b>how on earth</b> is it possible that in the world before the Crossing (which, from very numerous hints, we assume is ours) <b>there still was some undiscovered continent</b>? Maybe all the talking about seas and waters was metaphorical and the ships that made this Crossing were<i> space</i>ships? It is imperative that I be granted further explanation on this point because really, <b>I have no idea what went on there</b> and it's driving me nuts. Especially since this <b>post-apocalyptic medieval world</b>, for me, works. It definitely does. I'm just feeling the need to know <i>how</i> it came to be.<br /><br />•A big, colossal <b>no</b> to the lack of communication and basic information that went on throughout Kelsea's childhood and adolescence because I definitely do <i>not</i> see the point, if not that of adding some drama to the plot upon her finding out what is actually going on in her country. Seriously. No point. This is the kind of things that make me go ballistic.<br /><br />•<b>Anything else, I pretty much loved</b>. Finally we have a <b>strong-willed</b>, <b>tenacious</b> and <b>steadfast</b> heroine, one who won't apologize for her straightforwardness, one who won't back off when faced with the need to prioritize and make sacrifices, one who is not scared to <i>really</i> get her hands dirty and<b> shoulder her responsibilities</b>. I am extremely, extremely pleased with her and her characterization, even though at the very beginning, just for a little while, it seemed to be rather tentative and half-hearted -which, now it's perfectly clear, was all planned to make her following development stand out even more. Her greatest asset is her mind. I second that.<br />And a special mention should also be given to her foster family: I came to fully appreciate their role only at the end, thanks to the episode Mace told Kelsea, and that will forever be remembered as the moment when I nearly choked on the lump that had formed in my throat. <br /><br />•Speaking of whom, <b>Mace aka Lazarus</b>. Four words, and they'd better do because otherwise I'd be at a loss for what to say: Love. Him. To. Pieces. I want him to get to the end of this journey safe and sound and happy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And how cute would it be if <i>he</i> were the father? Be still, my heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•My fear regarding this book was that I would be <b>bored</b>. Well, <b>I was not</b>. Never, not even for a moment. As you may know, often action-packed books tire me more than stories revolving about <b>politics and mind-games </b>and such. <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> is of the latter kind, and I loved that it was (though I see why others would find it slow and uneventful). <br /><br />➽ I am<b> itching</b> to get my hands on the second instalment (all the better if I'm provided the info I need about the Crossing, but mainly I want to see Kelsea kick the Red Queen's ass). I did not expect to enjoy this book so much, and far be it from me to complain -though I'll postpone the reading of the sequels because I need to pass my exams, and this story is so engaging, if I start them now I won't even touch my textbooks. <br />As far as I'm concerned, <i>The Queen of the Tearling</i> is absolutely, <b>wholeheartedly recommended</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14622522881192423917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1208293154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1208293154" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1208293154?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=someone-hold-me">someone-hold-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=philosophical">philosophical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=lovely-romance-but-not-central">lovely-romance-but-not-central</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=complex-hero-heroine">complex-hero-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=conspiracies">conspiracies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=finding-oneself">finding-oneself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1208293154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7321837039588777329"><strong>This book has rendered me speechless. Oh, my bloody god. </strong>If you could see me now, I'm already having withdrawals, because the moment I finished, the first thing I blurted out was, "<em>I need book two. STAT."</em><br/><br/><strong>I avoided this book like the plague.</strong> Shortly before its release, one star reviews were popping out left and right, many from my trusted friends who share the same likes and dislikes as me. Because of that, I didn't want to read it. It was absolutely at the bottom of my TBR, but the other day, I </span>
  <span id="freeText7321837039588777329" style="display:none"><strong>This book has rendered me speechless. Oh, my bloody god. </strong>If you could see me now, I'm already having withdrawals, because the moment I finished, the first thing I blurted out was, "<em>I need book two. STAT."</em><br /><br /><strong>I avoided this book like the plague.</strong> Shortly before its release, one star reviews were popping out left and right, many from my trusted friends who share the same likes and dislikes as me. Because of that, I didn't want to read it. It was absolutely at the bottom of my TBR, but the other day, I went to a bookstore. I grabbed a cup of coffee from the Starbucks corner on the 3rd floor, walked around, and saw this beautiful cover reaching out to me from its lonely shelf.<br /><br />And so, I bought it.<br /><br /><strong>#BestDecisionEver.</strong><br /><br /><strong>I totally adored this novel.</strong> I expected to hate it, to bash it, to go she-hulk on it, but the more I read, the more engrossed I became, until I was like "fuck you" to the rising sun and continued on reading despite the growing Gucci bags under my eyes. I may have lost precious beauty sleep over it, but I don't really care, because this is one of my favorite books right now. <strong>The plot was awesome, the political intrigue insane, the heroine phenomenal, and the romance? ALMOST NON-EXISTENT.</strong> Which made me ship two people aggressively, because there were hints and gestures and I yearned for them even more because <em>they weren't bloody enough. </em>Forgive me if I resemble a mad woman right now, but this book just truly blew my mind away at how awesome and riveting it was.<br /><br />First of all, Kelsea. If I were to put a list of my top ten heroines of all time, she no doubt would be one of them.<strong> She's brainy, intelligent, strong-willed and courageous in every sense of the word, facing with hard resolve the troubles and problems brought about by her inheriting a broken and corrupt kingdom. </strong>She was hidden away from the rest of the world for the first nineteen years of her life, and on her 19th birthday, is whisked away by a group of knights to escort her back to her kingdom where the nobles have everything to lose with her on the throne. I don't know about you, guys, but if that were me, I would've had a nervous breakdown.<br /><br />But not Kelsea! She may have been sheltered, hidden away in the deepest parts of a forest, but she was raised to be kind and to be fierce, to be sympathetic and to be just, to be cautious and to take action, all the traits that monarchs before her lacked, all the traits her kingdom needs.<strong> I absolutely love how she fought through her insecurities, how she proved wrong those who underestimated her, how she stood up and made a name for herself in a society where females were looked down upon, how she became the kind of role model girls should emulate. </strong>Yes, she is far from perfect, but she tries her best and she goes against the tides and the waves and the tsunamis with everything she has, and that, my friends, is admirable. Fucking admirable.<br /><br />And the political intrigue! There is enough here to make you giddy. <strong>The kingdom is broken beyond comprehension that it's hard to know who to trust and who to be wary of.</strong> There are certainly a lot of key players here that we would need to keep an eye on in the second book, which makes things so bloody exciting.<br /><br />I do have to say that the setting is very special, though. T<strong>he best description for it would be a <i>"backward future"</i>,</strong> where some disaster has fallen upon earth (which is not known yet) and the survivors went elsewhere and established a more medieval way of life. <strong>I'd understand if some people may see it as too vague, and it can feel that way sometimes, but in my case, this aspect never really bothered me that much because the characters and the plot were riveting enough to take my mind off that issue, which is quite a feat because I'm usually very anal about this! </strong>All I can say is, the way this book was written makes the slow reveal of the world a pleasant and leisurely experience. And I mean, come on, my mind was too occupied cheering and fretting for our awesome Kelsea! (wink wink, nudge nudge)<br /><br /><strong>And did you know that the romance here is almost non-existent?</strong> Of course, our Kelsea talks about how handsome her guards are, but as someone who hasn't seen many people in her life, you can't really blame her! And she may have a crush on a mysterious figure, but aside from these things, it doesn't take center stage at all. She is surrounded by knights, but they're the types who actually do their jobs and don't flirt around. They are all focused on their task, and that is to protect the Queen.<strong> Of course, there are many interactions between them, especially with Mace (the Captain of the Guard who is old enough to be her father) who she establishes a mentor-like relationship with and Pen (who is 11 years her senior) who is her close guard, but they never got close to cheesy.</strong> They are all meaningful interactions that are vital to her character development. But, that doesn't mean there aren't any hints! Of course there are, but they are far and few between, which makes it even better, because the shipper in me became aggressive hunting for them ;) It also made me even more excited for the next book!<br /><br />P.S. I ship her with Pen. OMG.<br /><br /><strong>All in all, Queen of the Tearling is awesome and I'm glad I gave it a chance, because last night this book gave me such a high like you wouldn't believe (check out my Twitter for my incoherent rave tweets). </strong>Where is my book two?!?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7321837039588777329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2033941922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033941922" />
    <a title="Nick Borrelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5427149-nick-borrelli"><img alt="Nick Borrelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603556851p2/5427149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033941922?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Borrelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Borrelli" href="/user/show/5427149-nick-borrelli">Nick Borrelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer7177107660102022838">I am so glad that I don't weigh other people's reviews heavily when I decide whether or not I am going to read a book. If I had, I probably would have never tried this series. As it happens, what I discovered was a deep, complex, interesting, and engaging post-apocalypse fantasy that I flew through in four days. It also shattered my expectations and made me want to immediately start book 3. Erika Johansen is one heck of a writer and I am anxious to see where she takes this series. Reading an int</span>
  <span id="freeText7177107660102022838" style="display:none">I am so glad that I don't weigh other people's reviews heavily when I decide whether or not I am going to read a book. If I had, I probably would have never tried this series. As it happens, what I discovered was a deep, complex, interesting, and engaging post-apocalypse fantasy that I flew through in four days. It also shattered my expectations and made me want to immediately start book 3. Erika Johansen is one heck of a writer and I am anxious to see where she takes this series. Reading an interview of her recently she states that one of the books will be a backstory and history of how the Tearling came about and what cataclysm occurred to force the people of a long ago time to flee and shun technology in favor of a medieval lifestyle. Tremendous! I can't wait.</span>

At that moment, Javel knew for certain that she truly was the Queen, though he never knew why or how he knew.”</i><br/><br/>Holy shit. That was the most beautiful thing I've read in such a long time.<br/>How is it possible that my heart feels broken and whole at the same time?<br/>My eyes wont stop watering yet I can't help but smile like a Cheshire Cat.<br/><br/>I had put this book off for so long and I'm kicking myself for not picking this up sooner!<br/><i>Seriously Taylor, what t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2721980886187855525" style="display:none"><b>5000/5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>“The Queen held up her hands for silence. At that moment, Javel knew for certain that she truly was the Queen, though he never knew why or how he knew.”</i><br /><br />Holy shit. That was the most beautiful thing I've read in such a long time.<br />How is it possible that my heart feels broken and whole at the same time?<br />My eyes wont stop watering yet I can't help but smile like a Cheshire Cat.<br /><br />I had put this book off for so long and I'm kicking myself for not picking this up sooner!<br /><i>Seriously Taylor, what the hell were you thinking you Bafoon??</i><br />This book has everything you want and need in a fantasy story; <b>Adventure, magical elements, whimsical characters</b> and a <i>world building like nothing else.</i><br />Did I mention the characters? <b>*sobs*</b><br /><br /><i>“My responsibility, she thought, and the idea brought no fear now, only an extraordinary sense of gratitude. <br />My kingdom.”</i><br /><br />This was the first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6953956.Erika_Johansen" title="Erika Johansen" rel="nofollow noopener">Erika Johansen</a> novel I've read and I can tell you now, it won't be the last. Her style of writing is just <i>utter perfection</i> and she already has a high ranking as one of my new favorite authors.<br /><br />From the very first page I was completely hooked and obsessed with this story and it was all I could think about in the 2 days it took me to read this.<br /><i>Legitimately, my day job came second to this book, and I'm not even sorry.</i><br />I feel like I am one of the only living human being who has jumped on this bandwagon last but if you're still yet to pick this book up, please, for heavens sake, stop what you're doing and pick this up.<br />It will undoubtedly be your new addiction.<br /><br /><i>Now to get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22698568.The_Invasion_of_the_Tearling__The_Queen_of_the_Tearling___2_" title="The Invasion of the Tearling (The Queen of the Tearling, #2) by Erika Johansen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invasion of the Tearling</a> and ugly cry over the pages.</i></span>

<div id="review_2085969518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085969518" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085969518?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085969518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8164994987620370834"><b>*** 3.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the MaChalos, since we are on a Yong Adult Summer Binge:) </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"...“Time stretched years back and years forward, but nothing that came afterward ever had the power to wash away what came before.”..."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I am not really in the mood to write a review, but I do need to say, that this is one Young Adult book with quite a bit of violence and violent content and innuendos in it. So, if I was a young person approaching this, I would have to ask myself if I am ready to read abou</span>
  <span id="freeText8164994987620370834" style="display:none"><b>*** 3.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the MaChalos, since we are on a Yong Adult Summer Binge:) </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Time stretched years back and years forward, but nothing that came afterward ever had the power to wash away what came before.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I am not really in the mood to write a review, but I do need to say, that this is one Young Adult book with quite a bit of violence and violent content and innuendos in it. So, if I was a young person approaching this, I would have to ask myself if I am ready to read about some things which tend to be typical for war-torn countries and experienced by the oppressed people. I am talking about everything from slavery, rape, child abuse, child sacrifice, and all of those up to murder by torching someone on fire... I know when I was very young, books with such content made me have nightmares and I just want to give people heads up. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“What does the Red Queen want, then?" Kelsea had asked Carlin. She had no interest in maps and wanted to wrap up the lesson.<br />"What conquerors always want, Kelsea: everything, with no end in sight.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Kelsea is the hair to the throne of the Tearling, a country in a land Americans and Brits have moved to after something catastrophic has happened to those countries. We are not told what exactly happened, but now, about 200 years later, in a country started by an utopic socialist but overtaken by a royalist regime, people live as if in the Dark Ages and very little of the old life has been transferred over. It does not seem like the Queens up to now have been very good at protecting their people, a fact made worse by the neighboring Queendom, where The Red Queen rules with magic and fear. This Queen had won a war with the Tearling and now, as a price for the peace treaty, the Tearling sends 300 people or more every month as a tax, many of those children, and all of them used and abused as slaves by the enemy. The new Queen has to figure out a way to make life better for her regular subjects, while trying to tame down the out of control corrupt and debouched nobility. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“...Javel saw evil in those bright blue eyes, not malevolence but something much worse: an evil born of lack of self-awareness, an evil that didn't know it was evil and therefore could justify anything.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />This quote is about our bad guy, who really doesn't think of himself as evil, explaining his deeds as <i>"Nothing personal, just business..."</i> O, how I hate this sentiment, echoing in our political reality today... However, we have some more complex characters, who know where the line is between keeping or completely loosing your soul, and those were the ones I actually enjoyed about reading. The loyal to the Queen guards and the Fetch, a possible love interest, a head of a gang of thieves, were quite interchangeable the way they were written, so I don't have much to say about them... For adults, and supposedly smart people, they did not come of as such in my opinion. And yes,m they are all great warriors and killers...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Not just a thief, but a murderer as well. Beneath the handsome man, Kelsea sensed another man, a terrible one, with a life as black as the water in an ice-covered lake. A murderer many, many times.<br />The idea should have brought horror. Kelsea waited for a long moment, bu what came instead was an even worse realization: it didn't matter at all.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />The story was very well told, but the book lacks in planning of the plot. I think, from what we have been shown in this first book in a trilogy, the author most probably started with some idea in mind, but could have used a bit more time in structuring the story in a way that would not have felt meandering at times. There is something to be said about less is more. There was a whole a lot of angst, compliments of our 19 year old heroine, newly come into the Queen's throne, having been hidden away for most of her childhood in order to save her life. We are told repeatedly she is not pretty, she is overweight, and she loves books, but has no real life experience in anything, so it is natural for her to have some insecurities. However, the wining her uncle and couple of the other characters subjected us to, was a bit of a overkill... We got it, not to bright, not getting reality, not understanding their evil... There are ways to say all of that and not go on and on, is all I am saying:) <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Time stretched years back and years forward, but nothing that came afterward ever had the power to wash away what came before.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />So, not a bad read and I am interested enough to want to know what happens after, but I think it definitely needs a certain mindset, and I don't think I was in it whilst I read it... It's not you, it is me kind of thing:) <br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you Need in the Pages of a Good Book!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8164994987620370834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
