          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388538383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6896563482337276856"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blotspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blotspot.com</a><br/><br/>Okay a few excerpts from the book before I get into it! <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"There's no other life for me. Anyway, clemency wouldn't begin to repay your debt. I've given you a greater gift than you know."<br/>"What gift?"<br/>"You'll find out. In return, I expect you to keep it safe."<br/>Kelsea turned back to the mirror. "Great God, tell me you didn't impregnate me while I slept."<br/>The Fetch threw back his head and roared with laughter. He placed a friendly hand on Kelsea's back, making her s</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText6896563482337276856" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blotspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blotspot.com</a><br><br>Okay a few excerpts from the book before I get into it! <br><br><b>
  <i>"There's no other life for me. Anyway, clemency wouldn't begin to repay your debt. I've given you a greater gift than you know."<br>"What gift?"<br>"You'll find out. In return, I expect you to keep it safe."<br>Kelsea turned back to the mirror. "Great God, tell me you didn't impregnate me while I slept."<br>The Fetch threw back his head and roared with laughter. He placed a friendly hand on Kelsea's back, making her skin prickle. "Tear Queen, you'll either be dead within a week or you'll be the most fearsome ruler this kingdom has ever known. I see no middle ground."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"I demand punishment, Majesty!" Lady Andrews had recovered her voice. "Give me that guard!"<br>Kelsea burst out laughing, true laughter that rang across the audience chamber. It felt wonderful, more so as Lady Andrew's face turned a bright, choleric purple. <br>"I'll tell you what to do, Lady Andrews. You take your dress and get the hell out of my Keep."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>She grabbed his arm, not hard, but not too gently either. "But make no mistake: if you ever refuse to obey a direct order of mine again, I will kill you. Anger almost made me do it once, and could easily make me do it again. I'm not a child any longer, Lazarus, nor am I a fool. I'm either the Queen or I'm not....there can be no grey."<br>Mace swallowed; she heard it clearly in the dark. "You're the Queen, Lady."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"My eyes are terrible. What is that?"<br>"That, Lady, is a head on a pike," replied Wellmer.<br>"Whose head?"<br>"Your uncle's Lady. I went down there just to make sure. The pike is hung with a placard that says 'A gift for the Tear Queen, compliments of the Fetch."<br>Despite the gruesome nature of the offering, Kelsea smiled. </i>
</b><br><br>OMG!!!!!!!! I freaking loved this book and it is on my favorite books list! Loved it! Loved it! Loved it! <br><br>So... all of her life until she turned 19, Kelsea was brought up by Carlin and Barty. They taught her as much as they could about being a future queen, not the fancy stuff, real life stuff. Her mother, Queen Elyssa sent her away as a baby to make sure she was safe. <br><br>One day the Queen's Guard came to get Kelsea and take her back to the Keep to take the throne. Her mother had been dead for some time, but I won't tell you about that. Kelsea's jerk of an uncle has been ruling in her mother's place and he is an arsehole beyond and back!! <br><br>Not all of the guards make it back as they have to split up since her uncle sent assassin's to kill her, told you he was an arsehole, but he is worse than you think. <br><br>My favorite out of this group is Lazarus who goes by Mace, he is tough as nails and has a sworn vow to the Queen. He's a very smart man and for some reason I kept picturing the Hound from Game of Thrones. Anyhoo... Kelsea makes him the Captain of the Guards. I love the banter these two have all through the book. There is a snark there and it's not like your typical Queen and Guard or servants, Kelsea is a nice person, well to those that deserve it at any rate. <br><br>Along the way to the Keep we get to meet some bandits/criminals with the Fetch as their leader. He is awesome too. I love his character and can't wait to find out who he is and what his deal is because he always wears a mask, although at one point some little thing was revealed and I need to know!! <br><br>I loved when they made their first appearance at the Keep and Kelsea stands up to some bad trade that is going down in her kingdom. She also has a little magic, but I won't tell you about that either :) Let's just say they made a fearsome sight at the top of the hill giving out orders. <br><br>This is a long book and it never got boring to me one time! I was just loving it the whole way through. I see that it's one of those books that people either hate or love and I'm a lover! <br><br>All of the trials that Kelsea was put through and came out on top and the better for it were awesome! <br><br>There is an evil Queen of Mortmesne (Red Queen) that the Tearling are going to have to battle and take out at some point. I'm anxious to see what happens in these next books with this evil, evil woman! <br><br>Oh yeah and I love the guard Pen too, he's a good guy. <br><br>I think the cover of the book is beautiful and it has a string bookmark inside. I kept forgetting and looking around for my bookmark, but I digress. Just awesome! If I could do gifs on here I would do a little dance at how much I loved this book :) Fin! <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/book%20banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437402575i/15581842._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo book banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6896563482337276856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_907386207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907386207" />
    <a title="Eva Müller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427680-eva-m-ller"><img alt="Eva Müller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428080468p2/3427680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907386207?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva Müller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva Müller" href="/user/show/3427680-eva-m-ller">Eva Müller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593072691" href="/book/show/17415882-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427680-eva-m-ller?shelf=dafuq-did-i-just-read">dafuq-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427680-eva-m-ller?shelf=stick-them-with-the-pointy-end">stick-them-with-the-pointy-end</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427680-eva-m-ller?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427680-eva-m-ller?shelf=death-by-boredom">death-by-boredom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427680-eva-m-ller?shelf=who-thought-this-was-a-good-idea">who-thought-this-was-a-good-idea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907386207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15301695882871265152">You can also find this review on <a href='http://bibliodaze.com/2014/05/review-the-queen-of-the-tearling-by-erica-johansen/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bibliodaze</a><br/><br/><i>The Queen of Tearling</i> has been called “a female <i>Game of Thrones</i>”. Before starting the book I wasn’t quite sure what they meant by that. After finishing I can only say that if there is such a thing as “a female Game of Thrones” this book is certainly not it because <i>The Queen of Tearling</i> pretty much manages to fail in every way imaginable.<br/><br/><b>First: The world-building.</b><br/><br/>We’re in a post-apocalyptic world. What exactly happened? When did it happen? How much time </span>
  <span id="freeText15301695882871265152" style="display:none">You can also find this review on <a href="http://bibliodaze.com/2014/05/review-the-queen-of-the-tearling-by-erica-johansen/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bibliodaze</a><br><br><i>The Queen of Tearling</i> has been called “a female <i>Game of Thrones</i>”. Before starting the book I wasn’t quite sure what they meant by that. After finishing I can only say that if there is such a thing as “a female Game of Thrones” this book is certainly not it because <i>The Queen of Tearling</i> pretty much manages to fail in every way imaginable.<br><br><b>First: The world-building.</b><br><br>We’re in a post-apocalyptic world. What exactly happened? When did it happen? How much time has passed since then? Who cares? It also takes a few chapters till you realize that this is a future world and not your average pseudo-medieval fantasy-setting because at first it looks a lot like one. The states we hear of are monarchies, the weapons used swords as well as bows and arrows and horses are the only means of transportation.<br><br>However the apocalypse can't have been that long ago because a lot knowledge about the technology still seems to exist. Kelsea even knows that e-readers were once a thing. Now people can’t even built a printing-press anymore… however they can do cosmetic surgery and organ-transplants. I was tempted to start a drinking-game for such world-building inconsistencies but my liver is not that strong.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399537700ra/9564406.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There is also The Crossing. At one point it is also referred to the British-American Crossing which should give you a vague hint about starting and landing point. It was lead by a guy called William Tearling and he also gave the new country his name. Why did they need new names for places? I have no idea. For a while I thought that perhaps the Crossing referred to some kind of space-expedition but it clearly must have been a voyage with actual ships (as somehow they thought it would be a smart idea to put all the doctors in one ship which then sank). So…has whatever apocalyptic event happened changed the earth so much that continents and borders as we know them don’t exist anymore? There is also mention of “uncharted territories” which are rather rare on this world. Is it perhaps set in space after all? Then how did all the technology for space-ships get lost? Read this book and get absolutely no answers to these questions!<br><br>More than once I got the impression that originally this was planned as a typical medieval-style fantasy and then last-minute some vague references to some dystopian settings were added. That would explain many of the inconsistencies also those about the role of the church and of women.<br><br>See: William Tearling was an Atheist. A quite strict one apparently. But in Kelsea’s Tearling the church is quite influential again. So influential that Kelsea will only really be accepted as Queen if she is crowned by a priest. What happened that the church gained so much power again? Don’t ask. Why would anybody care abut such minor things? (Drink…just drink)<br><br>Generally the church is very typically medieval-Catholic (even though it is described as mixture between Catholicism and a ‘post Crossing Protestant sect’…whatever that means). Only read the Bible and other religious texts, no worldly books, abortion is evil, who gets to be pope has more to do with politics than faith and so on. Now I’m the first to admit that the (Catholic) church is not exactly progressive but the apocalypse happens and all it does is catapult its views a few centuries back? I’d have expected some major changes.<br><br>It gets even more confusing when you try to figure out the role of women in this world. To give but one example, Kelsea’s mother became queen even though she had a younger brother. So we’re clearly in a world where inheritance rights don’t discriminate against women. Additionally nobody knows who Kelsea’s father is (a few know but won’t tell because of reasons) but there seems to be no issue with this. Everybody accepts her as queen.<br><br>Think about that: in (western) history you get a few queens who became rulers because there was no male offspring but an illegitimate offspring on the throne? With no knowledge of who the father is? Unthinkable. But not even the church objects and they usually are somewhat conservative in these matters.<br><br>To cut it short: if the royal claim can be passed through the female blood-line alone, that should indicate a pretty awesome setting with equal rights for men and women (most royal families today don’t even have that law) – except that it really isn’t.<br><br>The warriors/guards are all men, the women cook, care for the children, knit and weave (while men can’t even distinguish knitting-needles from a weaving-loom), and do all the other stereotypical female work. When Kelsea demands sword-training and an armour, the others look at her like she’s insane (even though an armour should really be no question considering how many people are trying to kill her), the captain of her army is reluctant to discuss strategy with a woman and we only ever meet churchmen, no female priests/bishops etc.<br><br>Drink some more before we get to:<br><br><b>Second: Logic. Or the lack thereof.</b><br><br>I won’t deny it. I have read fantasy-novels with bad world-building before and I’m able to overlook it if the rest of the book at least had a decent plot. This is clearly not the case here. Every single person is just extremely stupid. If they weren’t then the book might have been over in a third of the time.<br><br>Kelsea’s mother died when she was just a year old and out of fear for her life she was raised in exile. Her foster-parents did make sure she received an education. She knows a lot about ancient history (whatever that means in this world), she’s a fast reader and she can hunt and skin animals.<br><br>Go and pick out the skills that are important for somebody who needs to rule a whole country.<br><br>Yeah.<br><br>They barely told her anything about the current state of Tearling. Kelsea doesn’t even know how her mother died or what kind of ruler she was because… because… why would that be important? Later, when she is with her guard (who also served her mother), she asks them too but they all refuse to tell her. Then she actually asks how she is supposed to make good decisions if they don’t tell her what happened which might be the only smart thing she does in the whole book. The answer:<br><br><blockquote>“Why dwell on the past Lady? You have the power to make your own future.”</blockquote><br><br>I don’t know… Have you heard the phrase “Learning from past mistakes” before?<br><br>Speaking of the Queen’s Guard: they get drunk while on duty and fail to stop two assassination attempts on Kelsea (as well as one kidnapping). Only Jaime Lannister has a worse record of protecting royalty.<br><br><b>Third: This is not how to write likeable love-interests.</b><br><br>At one point Kelsea gets kidnapped by bandits (because of reasons…) As she’s injured she passes out quite quickly and when she wakes up again she notices that she has been cleaned and is wearing a new dress. When it turns out that the head of the bandits did this she is clearly uncomfortable. His reaction: smiling and telling her she has no need to worry because she’s too plain for him.<br><br>Yes. And a few days later she actually has a very similar conversation with him. Later she spends a lot of time day-dreaming about that guy because he’s so hot and charming…<br><br>That’s especially jarring as in the rest of the book we learn that pretty much every single bad guy is also a rapist. Just so we can be sure that they're really evil. But they’re also all ugly so it’s different. Hot guys are allowed to tell girls they're not pretty enough for them to even consider such a thing.<br><br>Is there alcohol left? Because I don’t even know what to say to that.<br><br><b>Fourth: There’s a plot somewhere</b><br><br>Mostly it involves Kelsea acting stupid and spoiled. She also has a Jewel of Plot Convenience that makes most decisions for her so she doesn’t need to worry. Who wants a protagonist who makes their own decisions anyway? It’s much more interesting if her magically jewellery actually drags her along and gives her powers as the plot demands so she's always protected. Otherwise this could get exiting and we don't want that.<br><br>ARC provided by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review</span>
  <a data-text-id="15301695882871265152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1163188310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1163188310" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1163188310?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062290366" href="/book/show/18712886-the-queen-of-the-tearling">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1163188310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2102164371058974760">This was an extraordinary book! I simply loved it! <br/>There are so many things that can be said about this story; so many aspects of it that I really admired, but if I have to settle on one thing that I admired the most, it was the protagonist Kelsey. What an amazing character! I loved her personality and how she changed to a reasonable, mature woman. I loved the fact that she wasn't a beauty; focus came to be on her inside and her decisions and not her looks. I also loved how she was so self-aware</span>
  <span id="freeText2102164371058974760" style="display:none">This was an extraordinary book! I simply loved it! <br />There are so many things that can be said about this story; so many aspects of it that I really admired, but if I have to settle on one thing that I admired the most, it was the protagonist Kelsey. What an amazing character! I loved her personality and how she changed to a reasonable, mature woman. I loved the fact that she wasn't a beauty; focus came to be on her inside and her decisions and not her looks. I also loved how she was so self-aware of her looks because that's how every woman would feel when being surrounded by beauties and strong men. Kelsey was a character that made me smile, cry and root for her and I definitely understand why Emma Watson wants to play her in a movie!<br />However, as I said there are so many other things about this story that made me very happy. It is very accessible, meaning that you can read it very easily without getting caught in great, fantastical descriptions that you have a hard time understanding. Basically, Erika Johansen does an excellent job at describing everything so that I could imagine this world vividly. <br />I also loved how the POV shifts during the story. Kelsea is our main character but it was so interesting to see behind the enemy's lines which furthermore increased the tension. <br />The only unfortunate thing about this story was the fact that we never encounter the real danger (without saying too much!). I assume this will be the first installment in a series, but I missed some more chapters on the dark side and I would've loved to have more of a resolution from this single book. <br />A funny thing about this fantasy story is that it reaches beyond the genre: It contains so many references to things from our modern world that you don't normally encounter in fantasy worlds: e.g. there is talk of birth control and J. K. Rowling. I found that fascinating while also being a bit confused as to where to place this story on a timeline. <br />But all in all, a FANTASTIC story! This is fantasy at its best because it contains some breathtaking scenes, amazing characters and a very tense and intriguing plot. This is definitely a book I would recommend :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2102164371058974760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GX4aB5Y7jQGGt2sgBuEoCIYfWelAnP3aa5jD42JVj8cjWHPVLWVEaSGc30HxFCLXUEC+IY4Rc70w5oVSrxZ9XQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cJvpKDl1XrGdS7I4z4HYOaGGspp9/1/+BHsoKQWoU79KvYD6giuX2TpgBlk4dNLmd9lVUrNy0ZlfBW6YyOuhJQ==')})
  }

For the warrior tells her a new tale: across hot, windswept sands teeming with creatures of fire, and rivers where the mythical marid sleep; past ruins of once-magnificent human metropolises, and mountains where the circling hawks are not what they seem, lies Daevabad, the legendary city of brass, a city to which Nahri is irrevocably bound. \n\nIn that city, behind gilded brass walls laced with enchantments, behind the six gates of the six djinn tribes, old resentments are simmering. And when Nahri decides to enter this world, she learns that true power is fierce and brutal. That magic cannot shield her from the dangerous web of court politics.
